The Social Basis of Fascism (Part 2)

— Written by Joseph Barnes, translated by Bu Ren

Certainly, this petty bourgeoisie has organized intermittent resistance to the control of trust capital. It has attacked combines, just as the Luddite riots in England did a hundred years ago. It has organized various political revolutions under different forms of populist banners. The social and economic philosophy of Thomas Jefferson—perhaps the most complete and formulaic political expression representing the petty bourgeoisie—has never left American life. The American anti-monopoly movement, with its slogan of "Down with the trusts," laws against chain stores, the political tradition represented by Judge Brandeis, the idiom of "cursing the big capitalists," and the cooperative movement, all sufficiently prove the power of this tradition.

However, it is worth noting that after it overthrew feudalism, there have been few clear successes. The town merchant who bought property in "The Cherry Orchard" was already excluded by the lumber enterprises in Galilee before he could directly sell timber. The tremendous pressure of the machine age, tending towards unification, trustification, and large-scale production and distribution of goods, devastates the original interests of the middle class, just as it devastates the economic and social principles propagated by its leaders.

This fate has always been attached to the very structure of the so-called middle class. Its efforts to construct a rational and viable system have been hampered from the outset by the fact that its nature is neither the same as that of the trust bourgeoisie nor the same as that of the proletariat. It is a mixture of various elements, some of which are clearly in conflict with each other.

One result of this is that in the last eighty years, the middle class has played the difficult role of mediating between trust capital and the proletariat. This is a role that the landlord class of the old European feudal system successfully played for several years. Bismarck's economic laws, like Stolypin's economic laws in Russia, were clever schemes used by the remnants of the feudal aristocracy to restrain the predatory ambitions of the nouveau riche capitalist class. President Roosevelt, if he represented the weak American landowning aristocracy, could be in a similar position. However, it is much more reasonable to see most of the recovery plan as an effort by the American petty bourgeoisie to defend itself against organized labor on the one hand and rapacious financial capitalism on the other.

Until now, the middle class in democratic industrial countries has only succeeded in maintaining itself. Beyond that, it has had no success. In America, as in Western Europe, the odds are stacked in favor of trust monopolists. Financial and industrial concentration has only progressed and not regressed. The free competition in the open market assumed by Adam Smith remains, after more than two hundred years, nothing more than an assumption.

This is the social background that must be understood to clarify the rise of fascist groups in Western Europe. Whether in Italy or Germany, especially before the rise of fascism, fascists clearly and directly appealed to the middle class. They cursed the trade unions led by Moscow, cursed "international," "Jewish," or "large-scale" capital. Mussolini's Blackshirts found their earliest and greatest strength in the center of the peninsula, in the farmers between the southern and northern industrial areas, in regions where the petty bourgeoisie and tenant farmers predominated—these Italians were formed into the middle class by the constraints of tradition and material interests. In Germany, the situation was exactly the same. Individuals of various "forgotten" types of this class, whether urban or rural, Catholic or Protestant, sent Mussolini and Hitler to positions of power.

Once in power, the forgotten people were forgotten again. In Italy, the "end of the capitalist era" is still often heard in speeches, but the relative position of the middle class in the distribution of national wealth or income has not changed much, and large enterprises have continued to develop. Before 1933, National Socialists would smash the windows of department stores in Berlin; but since 1933, no specific laws have been enacted to help small merchants resist their large competitors. The middle-class movement under National Socialism has been stopped by its leaders because this movement has become a cause of displeasure to them.

Fascism initially appealed to the middle class to gain power, and then used that power for the benefit of large-scale monopoly interests. This contradiction inherent in fascism has two very different explanations. One is the fascists' own explanation. The other is the socialists' explanation.

From the fascists' point of view, the connection between the fascist state and private enterprise is only part of a larger concept. This is the corporate state. It endows the entire sacred concept of the state with an entity that transcends the interests of individuals and groups. It contains a demand for feelings of sacrifice, in that it clearly recognizes the need to temporarily suffer for the sake of the state. In addition, it contains a demand for long-term encouragement, in that it anticipates the glory of national victory that exceeds the reward of initial sacrifices. In Italy, this dismal management of the corporate state is considered an experiment; organizing corporations to peacefully integrate the separate interests of the masses is only a recent thing. A sympathetic writer explained it this way: "The separate contributions of each social class in the production process should be determined not only by their respective strengths, but also by harmony based on the principles of mutual understanding and equitable equality. This is the Fascist ideal."

New Swedish Chargé d'Affaires, Phyllis, Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday

Baron Johan Beck-Frus, the newly appointed Swedish Chargé d'Affaires to China and Consul-General in Shanghai, arrived in Shanghai at 2:00 PM yesterday on the Dollar Line's President Hoover, which docked at Pontoons No. 11 and 12 in Yangshupu. Among those who went to the pier to welcome him were the acting Consul-General of Sweden in Shanghai, Mr. Hartman, and many overseas merchants. Aviation Youth Studying in France, Cao Shi, Returns to China and Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday. Claims French Air Force is Improving Daily. Will Report to Capital Before Returning to Hunan to Visit Relatives

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, Mr. Cao Shiang, a young Chinese aviator who traveled abroad, a native of Hunan, went to France in 1930 and first entered the Paris Civil Aviation Academy. After graduating, he entered the Lyon National Military Aviation Academy in France, specializing in various subjects such as driving, manufacturing, repairing, and bombing techniques. During the Shanghai War in 1932, he returned to China to visit his relatives and was warmly welcomed by all sectors. Later, he was specially appointed by the French government as a member of the French Aeronautical Society and went to France. This spring, he was hired as an aviation instructor with the rank of colonel in the 35th Air Brigade. He has represented France in international aviation competitions and has received a military honor medal from the National Military Council. He is truly one of the outstanding talents among Chinese students studying aviation abroad.

Returned to China Yesterday

Mr. Cao recently became aware of the lack of aviation technicians in China, and because he had not returned to his homeland for several years, he was very unfamiliar with the situation in the country. Therefore, he decided to return to China. On the 3rd of last month, he left France from Marseilles on the French mail steamer General Xiafei and arrived in Shanghai at 1:30 PM yesterday. Those who went to the port to welcome him included representatives from the Hunan Provincial Government and Cao's relatives and friends Nie Haifan, Liu Guoxian, Cao Linchuan, Huang Gede, Liu Guoxing, Miss Wang Ke, and more than 30 foreign friends. The French military also specially dispatched two soldiers to escort Mr. Cao to China. After arriving at the port, he was accompanied by Nie Haifan and others to his residence to rest. In the evening at 7:00 PM, Nie held a welcoming dinner for Mr. Cao at the YMCA and invited relatives and friends to accompany him. The party broke up at about 9:00 PM. Mr. Cao plans to stay in Shanghai for a week. If he has the opportunity, he plans to demonstrate his flying skills in Shanghai, and then go to the capital to pay his respects to the authorities, make a report, and return to Hunan to visit his relatives.

Delivers Speech

Yesterday, a reporter from the Shen Shi News Agency visited Mr. Cao at the YMCA. Through the introduction of Mr. Nie Haifan, he met the young aviator. Mr. Cao is of medium stature and was wearing a French military uniform. According to him, he went to study in France when he was 19 years old. French language is difficult to learn, and the cost of living is higher than in England, America, Italy, and other countries. An ordinary meal costs about two yuan in national currency, so life in France was quite hard. After being appointed as an aviation instructor, his monthly income was 500 yuan in national currency. This time, he originally planned to buy his own plane and fly back to China to fulfill his long-distance flying wish, but due to the tense situation in Europe, flying was inconvenient, so he returned by sea. The two soldiers sent by the French military to accompany him to China planned to return to France immediately because Mr. Cao's stay in China was uncertain. When asked about the tense relations between Germany and France, and what preparations the French government was making, he said that although he had been in France for a long time and worked in the military, he was very clear about it, but since it was an international issue, he would not elaborate.

French Air Force

Finally, Mr. Cao said that the aircraft of the French Air Force are improving daily. The latest fighter aircraft can climb straight up to 6,000 meters, has 3,000 horsepower, can carry seven people and a huge amount of 500 pounds of bombs, and three twin machine guns. The most peculiar thing is that there is a camera installed on the head of the machine gun. The direction in which the bullets are fired, how the enemy plane is hit, and how the fuselage is destroyed can all be captured on camera. French aviation training is quite expensive. Military aircraft cost 230 yuan per hour to teach, while civilian aircraft cost 70 yuan per hour. Speaking of personal life, he said that he does not drink or smoke and is not engaged.

His stay in China is set at ten months, researching various agricultural products

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, the Ministry of Industry believes that the yields of China's main agricultural products, such as rice, wheat, and cotton, have declined in recent years, which are insufficient to meet the needs of the country, resulting in a large amount of imported grain, rice, and cotton. Fish Market Regulations Promulgated by the Ministry of Industry Yesterday

The Central News Agency, Nanjing, 7th. The Ministry of Industry announced the Shanghai Fish Market Regulations on the 7th, totaling nine chapters and forty-nine articles. The regulations stipulate that the share capital is 1.2 million yuan, divided into 12,000 shares, each share being 100 yuan in national currency, with official and commercial shares being half each. If the commercial shares are insufficient, they will be temporarily advanced by the government and sold successively, but the commercial shares must be paid at least 300,000 yuan first. As for the organization of the market, there will be eleven directors, and the Ministry of Industry will designate one of the standing directors as the chairman. There will be five supervisors, who will elect one person as the resident supervisor. There will also be a general manager and one or two deputy managers. The market will operate on the basis of public auctions and gradually reduce commissions to reduce the burden on fish merchants and fishermen. The shares can now be collected in full, and the shareholders' meeting will be held in Shanghai on the 9th. Wu Dingchang will go to Shanghai on the 8th to participate, and the opening ceremony can be held on the 19th.

Tricolor Ship on Fire, Shanghai Office Inquires About Truth

The William Bubor Line, managed by the local Tianxiang Shipping Company, has built several ships with the character "Tai" in the Far East Line in New York, namely the Taiping, Pacific, Taiyin, and Taiyang. Each ship is an express class. From Shanghai to New York, crossing the Pacific Ocean and passing through Panama, it takes only 37 days, which is the fastest ship in Shanghai, so the business is excellent. There is a departure every four weeks. The schedule was originally for the Taiyin, but due to major repairs in the dock, the line changed the ship and sent the Tricolor to China for the first time. It departed from Shanghai on March 23.

Large Amount of Goods Transported

The Tricolor originally sailed in the Atlantic Ocean. The ship is in excellent condition, has strong speed, and has passenger seats. This time, it returned to the United States from the Far East, carrying a large amount of cargo, originally 11,700 tons. Later, due to the shortage of 700 tons of tung oil in Shanghai, it could not be loaded on the ship. Therefore, it transported a total of 11,000 tons of export goods from the ports of Little Luzon, Hong Kong, Shanghai, and Japan, including wood, brown rope, cotton, silk waste, and wool. The ship was fully loaded with goods in each cabin. Most of the passengers disembarked in Luzon, and only two people disembarked in Shanghai.

Cause of Fire

Yesterday, a reporter from this newspaper went to the Tianxiang Shipping Company to ask its person in charge. According to him, Shanghai had not received a telegram after the Tricolor departed, because it was safe along the way. It was not until yesterday that the company learned from the newspaper that the ship had been burned. However, there has been no telegram from the voyage, probably because it is far from Shanghai and close to the United States, so the news was not sent to Shanghai. It is presumed that the cause of the fire started from the cotton, because the fire started in the fifth cabin, which contained cotton, and cotton is the most flammable.

All Shanghai Goods Lost

The goods from Shanghai were all loaded in the fifth cabin and on the deck, so they were the first to bear the brunt. According to reliable news received in Shanghai yesterday, 150 of the 500 bales of cotton have been burned (the remaining 350 bales are also unlikely to be salvaged), 137 bales of wool, 400 bales of walnuts, 30 bales of silk waste, 17 bales of pig bristles, and dozens of other sundry goods. Once ignited, it turned into a prairie fire, and all were scorched earth. The magnitude of the loss cannot be counted.

Inquiring About the Truth

The location of the fire is said to be about 1,000 nautical miles away from Yokohama, Japan, and has not yet reached Honolulu. The ship will now be stranded on the north Pacific coast. Tianxiang telegraphed the United States yesterday to inquire about the truth. The ship was originally scheduled to sail two trips to China. The second trip was scheduled to depart from Shanghai on August 21, but now another ship will be sent. The shipowner is Norwegian, named Torvtoft. Captain Taft has just been transferred from Hong Kong to the ship.

The National News Agency, Jiuyushan, 6th. Last Saturday, after the Baber Qian Line's Tricolor steamship caught fire, all thirteen passengers were transported to other ships by lifeboat, but there were still 45 sailors on board who are now trying their best to put out the fire. However, the fire is getting worse day by day. The ship is now in the waters 500 miles northwest of Midway Island, trying to reach Honolulu. However, according to a telegram from the Dollar Line's President Grant, the fire on the ship is fierce and the voyage is very slow.

Sichuan River Water Rises, Vessel Navigation Opens. Direct Shipping from Shanghai to Chongqing

Freight Transportation Begins Today, Totaling Three Vessels Upstream

The Sichuan River waterway has been shallow this year. In the Yichang area, the shallowest water level is only one inch above the bottom, causing merchant vessels from China, Britain, Italy, France, and Japan navigating the Sichuan River to suspend navigation. Although the water level has risen slightly since then, it is still only possible to navigate shallow-water passenger ships and cannot transport cargo through Yichang. In fact, Sichuan River cargo transportation has not been possible. It was not until the 4th of this month that the Sanbei Company received a telegram from Yichang stating that the Sichuan River water had risen, with the highest point being 2 feet 8 inches to 3 feet or more (excluding the bottom). It is estimated that on the 6th of this month, it will be possible to transport cargo through the shallow areas above Yichang. Jardine Matheson and Nissin and others also received news of the rising water. Therefore, they urgently dispatched the Jiahe (Jardine Matheson) and Changyang Maru (Nissin) vessels. The Jufu Company also sent the Fuyuan vessel to transport Sichuan cargo from Shanghai directly to Chongqing today. This is the first time since the Sichuan River water has been shallow and navigation has been interrupted that Shanghai has directly shipped fully loaded cargo into Sichuan.

According to Shiye News Agency, the four periodic account settlements, which Shanghai industry and commerce must go through every year in the fourth quarter, fifth quarter, tenth quarter, and year-end, are extraordinary periods of financial emergency for the city. We are now less than three weeks away from the fourth quarter, and most industries are already planning and fully preparing. According to the reporter's investigation, most banks and money shops can make a profit due to recent business development. Due to the bumper harvests in rural areas last year, the purchasing power of the people has increased, and sales are gradually booming in industries such as yarn, flower, rice, wheat, flour, grain, and cotton cloth. The import and export industries and various commercial firms have the most profits in non-ferrous metals, mineral sands, and pigments. Other commodities are also showing signs of recovery. It is hoped that the fourth quarter difficulty can be weathered steadily.

The Committee Lends as Much as Possible

The Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Loan Committee, because the Ministry of Finance approved the request of industry leaders last year, ordered each bank to identify 4.75 million yuan and each Qianye shop to identify 250,000 yuan, totaling 5 million yuan. After hiring industry giants to organize and establish before the fourth quarter, they immediately complied with the order to handle credit small loans for each industry to provide working capital. By the end of last month, more than 1.7 million yuan had been loaned out, the work was smooth, and the results were outstanding. The committee, in view of the financial storm that occurred in Shanghai in the fourth quarter of last year, has now decided to grant as many loans as possible before the fourth quarter of this year in order to thoroughly relieve the market, with a view to supporting industry and commerce and increasing work efficiency. It is heard that the number of industries applying for loans to the committee these days is much more enthusiastic than in the past. The committee will soon hold a meeting to review and approve loans. It is expected that the market's finances will be loosened after this.

Expand Lending and Overdrafts

Since the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications in this city concentrated 20 million yuan to carry out interbank lending at the time of the year-end closing of each industry last year, the financial industry has benefited a lot. Because the industrial and commercial fourth quarter is approaching, the expansion of this lending business has been carefully considered to help maintain the serious difficulties of future work. As for other banks, in addition to preparing work early and strengthening their own foundations, they have also actively handled current credit overdraft loans to provide relief to the market. Considerable plans have also been decided for various mortgage and goods loans.

Qianye will Discuss the Internal Board

In view of the fact that the 49 member shops of the Qianye Association have been deeply wary of their own preparations since the storm that occurred in the fourth quarter of last year, they have all followed the instructions of the Qianye Supervisory Committee. There should be no problems in the fourth quarter of this year. Yesterday, a Shiye News Agency reporter inquired from Qianye that each shop had made sufficient preparations for the fourth quarter. For all long-term loans, where the other party has excellent credit, an extension of the interest payment will be approved as much as possible. The fourth quarter "internal board" meeting is scheduled to be held at the same time as the executive committee meeting on the 25th of this month. These days, the revenue and expenses of each shop are not very busy. Yesterday afternoon in the Qianye market, the foreign exchange rate was stable at eight cents due to the lack of demand from all parties, that is, eight cents of interest per thousand yuan per day. It is heard that the foreign exchange rate is likely to increase step by step after this.

Postal Savings Bureau Absorbing Savings – Deciding on Three Principles

Simultaneous Emphasis on Safety, Liquidity, and High Interest – National Savings Reaching 50 Million Yuan

According to the Da Kung She, postal savings were first established in the eighth year of the Republic (1919), managed concurrently by post offices. In the nineteenth year of the Republic (1930), the system was slightly changed, with the savings and remittance sections being separated and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau established to handle savings and remittance businesses. Over the years, the public, recognizing the security and reliability of this form of savings, and that it is managed by the state, unlike ordinary commercial savings banks, has increased their savings accounts year by year. The minimum deposit for opening an account is one yuan, and the maximum limit is three thousand yuan for individuals and four thousand yuan for organizations. Over seven hundred postal districts nationwide handle savings. According to the bureau's recent statistics, there are over two hundred thousand savings account holders, with total savings reaching over fifty million yuan.

Three Investment Principles

According to Zhang Liangwu, the director of the Savings Department, postal savings have been established for many years and have a considerable history. Due to the limitations on the amount of savings, deposits have only reached over fifty million yuan. This is because large depositors tend to deposit and withdraw funds frequently, which is not in line with the purpose of savings. Postal services cannot utilize these funds, which would hinder the interests of small depositors. In the past, many commercial banks that faced economic stagnation were mostly affected by large depositors. If postal savings did not limit the amount of savings and accepted as much as possible, the savings could reach tens of millions. Therefore, the difference between postal savings and commercial savings lies in this aspect. Currently, the purpose of postal savings is to utilize funds and make reliable investments to protect the interests of depositors, thereby encouraging savings. Therefore, the bureau has recently decided on the following principles for savings investment methods: 1. Safety and reliability; 2. Capital liquidity; 3. Favorable interest rates. These three major principles will be implemented simultaneously to avoid speculative investments, ensure the benefits of postal savings, and promote the prosperity of the national economy. This is the mission and responsibility of the bureau.

International Remittance Business

The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau handled international remittances. In the twenty-second year of the Republic (1933), remittances totaled 1,518,880.55 yuan, and payments totaled 1,930,846.25 yuan. In the twenty-third year (1934), remittances totaled 1,582,190.09 yuan, and payments totaled 2,328,897.36 yuan. In the first half of the twenty-fourth year (1935) (from July to December), remittances totaled 700,671 yuan, and payments totaled 1,285,309 yuan. Currently, the domestic postal remittance area has been expanded by the Ministry of Communications to over 170 locations, allowing direct remittances with over 20 countries, including England, France, the United States, Belgium, Germany, Japan, Poland, Denmark, and India. It is expected that the amount of international remittances in the second half of the year will increase significantly.

Telephone Problem Committee – Protesting Telephone Rate Increases

Suggesting the Ratepayers Association Submit to the General Meeting for Discussion – Also Writing to Various Organizations to Lead the Protest Jointly

According to the Da Kung She, the Special District Telephone Problem Committee, after a routine meeting the other day, decided to expand its internal organization for long-term protest and appointed eleven organizations, including the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, as standing directors responsible for leading all users in the city to fight together. The committee also intends to draft protest measures and yesterday sent a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Concession, requesting that it be submitted to the Ratepayers' Representative Assembly on the 15th of this month for discussion. It also sent separate letters to the trade associations and the Citizens' Federation, requesting that they uniformly follow the telephone measures discussed by the committee in order to achieve victory. Details are as follows:

Letter Requesting Protest

The Special District Telephone Problem Committee yesterday sent letters to eleven organizations, including the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession, the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the French Concession, the Citizens' Federation of various districts, the Lawyers' Association, the Accountants' Association, the Journalists' Association, the Brokers' Association of the Five Exchanges, the Ningbo Native Place Association, the Pudong Native Place Association, and the Guangdong Native Place Association, requesting them to serve as standing directors and lead the protest. The letter stated, "Dear Sirs, our committee was established by various public organizations in the city and has been in existence for two months. Regarding the issue of Shanghai Telephone Company's rate increase, despite repeated appeals, the company is blinded by profit and disregards public opinion, resulting in the protest not being resolved to this day. With the approach of March telephone bills, users are sending inquiries in droves. Our committee feels that without concrete action, it cannot prompt the company to reflect. The sixth board of directors meeting decided to establish a standing board of directors to handle daily affairs and lead users to protest jointly. Therefore, we hereby send this letter, requesting that you immediately send the name of a representative to the committee so that we can hold a meeting on a regular basis. This matter concerns all citizens, so please do not neglect it."

Suggestion to the General Meeting

The 15th session of the World Taxpayers' Association Representative Assembly will be held on the 15th of this month. The committee yesterday drafted opinions against the telephone rate increase and requested that they be submitted to the Representative Assembly for discussion. The letter stated, "Dear Sirs, regarding the issue of the Shanghai Telephone Company's rate increase, which your association will submit to the Taxpayers' Representative Assembly for discussion, our association hereby submits the following opinions for consideration by the General Meeting: 1. Acknowledge the Shanghai Telephone Company's decision to charge, but charge three cents for both basic and excess calls; 2. Each telephone must be equipped with a meter (as some users have recently reported inaccurate counting by the company) and must be installed within three months; 3. Question the Board of Directors of the Municipal Council regarding the approval of rate increases for public utilities, which should not be handled unilaterally; 4. Send a letter to the Municipal Council, ordering the company to reduce expenses and not arbitrarily increase the burden on citizens; 5. If the company does not accept the three-cent per call calculation, telephone fees will be remitted to the Municipal Council for payment, and the Municipal Council shall be responsible for any line breaks or accidents; 6. The Ratepayers' Association shall be responsible for leading users in various districts to organize a telephone users' association to facilitate command and joint protest. The above suggestions are feasible, and we hope that they will be submitted to the General Meeting for discussion, for the public good."

Consistent Action

The committee yesterday also sent separate letters to the trade associations and the Citizens' Federation of various districts, requesting that they uniformly transfer the resolutions of the committee to all members for joint compliance and consistent action. The letter stated, "Dear Sirs, our association was established to protest the telephone rate increase, so its strength depends entirely on the support and cooperation of various public organizations. Currently, the Shanghai Telephone Company has refused to consider our association's suggestions for reducing telephone rates, resulting in the appeals not being resolved to this day. To prepare for long-term protest, we have strengthened our internal organization. Hereafter, all righteous actions of our association, which concern the interests of all users, must be uniformly notified and complied with to prompt the company to reflect. In addition to temporarily copying and announcing the resolutions, we hereby send this letter, hoping that you will take note and act accordingly. Best regards to all organizations."

Ministry of Industry – Establishing a Commodity Inspection Branch in Chongqing

Dispatching Zhang Weiru, Technical Expert from Shanghai Bureau, as Director – Officially Established on the 5th, Inspection to Commence on the 15th

Chongqing, located in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, is a central hub for the export of Sichuan native products, such as tung oil, bristles, and cow and sheep hides, which are concentrated there for transportation and re-export in large quantities. However, the quality varies, hindering the development of Sichuan's native product exports. Recognizing this, the Ministry of Industry has established a commodity inspection branch of the Hankou Commodity Inspection Bureau in Chongqing, dispatching Zhang Weiru, the head of the Chemical Products Inspection Group of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, as the director of the branch. The main internal personnel are mostly transferred from the Shanghai and Hankou bureaus, initially focusing on tung oil, cow and sheep hides, and bristles. Other commodities will be inspected as needed, with efforts to improve the quality of related commodities to maintain the reputation of Sichuan's special products. It is reported that the branch was officially established on April 5th and will commence inspection on the 15th. The address is located at [Address Missing].

Customs Penalty Cases – Law of Administrative Appeal Not Applicable

The Jianghai Customs has issued Announcement No. 1506, stating that merchants who wish to express objections or appeals against the penalties imposed by the Customs in accordance with the Regulations for the Prevention of Smuggling may not invoke the Law of Administrative Appeal. The announcement stated, "The organizational regulations and operating rules of the Customs Penalty Review Board were announced in Announcement No. 1418 posted on January 5, 1935. We have received an order from the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance stating that if merchants wish to express objections or file administrative lawsuits against the penalties imposed by the Customs Commissioner in accordance with the Regulations for the Prevention of Smuggling, they shall follow the procedures prescribed in Articles 28, 31, and 32 of the said Regulations and may not invoke the Law of Administrative Appeal. All merchants shall comply accordingly. This announcement is hereby issued. Superintendent Tang Hai'an, Customs Commissioner Pa Renshen."

Wang Fu Nail Factory Experiences Labor Dispute – Caused by Factory Increasing Working Hours

According to the Da Kung She, the Wang Fu Domestic Goods Nail Factory on Pinlang Road in West Shanghai has been open for three years and its business is quite developed, employing more than 100 workers. The factory is divided into day and night shifts, and the shifts are changed every 15 days. Recently, the factory suddenly increased the working hours of workers on the night shift to 12 hours, and added six more hours of work to each worker when changing shifts. Those who did not obey would have their wages deducted. Therefore, all the workers found it difficult to accept, and sent representatives to request the factory to change this policy, but they were rejected and the representatives were dismissed. This aroused public outrage, and the workers went on strike at 6:00 PM yesterday. Currently, because the workers do not have a union, they have automatically jointly petitioned the municipal party and government agencies for assistance.

Municipal Federation Petitions Executive Yuan – To Return Wang Bin Yan's Military Advance Payments – Please Forward Order to the Ministry of Finance for Repayment to Avoid Burden

According to the Da Kung She, the Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of this city presented a petition to the Executive Yuan yesterday, requesting that the Ministry of Finance be ordered to return the military advance payments handled by Wang Bin Yan, so as to avoid being burdened. The original presentation states: "This presentation is for requesting the Executive Yuan to order the Ministry of Finance to return the military advance payments handled by Shanghai gentleman Wang Bin Yan, so as to avoid being burdened due to public service. It is based on the report of the 16th District Branch, which states that Wang Bin Yan, a gentleman from Zhabei, is enthusiastic about public welfare, cares for the local area, and has a benevolent style that is admirable. In the 13th year of the Republic of China (1924), during the Jiangsu-Zhejiang War, the troops retreated to Zhabei. In order to raise funds for military use and handle local relief matters, he mortgaged his private houses and properties to banks and money houses for huge amounts of money to meet the needs of the time. Now, Guangdong Bank and others, as creditors, are pursuing debts in court. On March 23, the court sealed Wang's residence. It is found that the money borrowed was indeed used for military purposes and to protect the local area, and at that time the government promised to repay it, which is on record, and there is no obligation to have individuals bear the burden. Now, Wang is suffering the consequences of being homeless because of his love for the local area. Not only is Mr. Wang personally suffering injustice, but those who act righteously and bravely will be deterred. This case is of great importance. We urge your association to lead the citizens to uphold justice for Mr. Wang's burden due to public service and request that you present a petition to the Ministry of Finance immediately to have the military advance payments repaid as soon as possible in order to clear the litigation. The association submitted it to the 17th Executive Committee meeting, which recognized that the allegations were true and presented the petition to the Executive Yuan, requesting that the Ministry of Finance approve the repayment of the military advance payments handled by Mr. Wang to avoid burden and benefit public opinion. Respectfully presented to Jiang, the President of the Executive Yuan."

Overview of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association – A New Hospital Added in the Western District – Self-Management of Rickshaw Pullers' Insurance

The Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association held its 28th board meeting at the Western District Hall the other day. At the same time, the association had just established a new hospital in the Western District Hall with 12 beds, so the board members inspected the hospital at the beginning of the meeting. Then, they convened a meeting to discuss the work reports of various departments. According to the association's statistics for February, various association affairs related to the interests of rickshaw pullers have become increasingly developed compared to the previous month. Noteworthy aspects include: the number of consultations at the clinic in February reached more than 19,000, exceeding the previous month by more than 3,300; relief matters also increased from 1,848 cases in the previous month to 2,551 cases; in terms of donations, the association's various district halls received a total of nine plaques donated by rickshaw pullers, all of which were automatic expressions of gratitude from the beneficiary rickshaw pullers. In addition, Mr. Jin Fusu, the chief doctor of the Mutual Aid Association, donated a complete set of 12 hospital beds to the Western District Hall Hospital, and other benefactors donated tea cans and 25 yuan in cash, all of which have been gratefully acknowledged by the association. According to the report of the association's Labour Affairs Committee, it has been decided to purchase two public cemetery sites, each of five or six mu, in both the South Shanghai and North Shanghai areas, and build a tomb house on each site for burial and sacrifice purposes. In addition, it is planned to open a rickshaw pullers' savings bank, which has been approved in principle, but the details have not yet been drafted and will be reported later. Furthermore, the Medical Committee plans to add two doctors to meet the needs of rickshaw pullers who are seriously ill and need home visits, and also needs to add one nurse and one obstetric nurse to provide timely consultations to the families of rickshaw pullers. In addition, the Insurance Committee has also drafted an insurance plan for rickshaw pullers, deciding to manage it themselves. The Management Committee will first withdraw 30,000 yuan and deposit it into the bank's insurance account, and another insurance board of directors will be established, with all members of the existing Insurance Committee and one member of the Management Committee in charge of its incoming and outgoing funds. As for the original plan, major insurance companies in this city had previously issued insurance premium price lists, but after review by the committee, it was felt that the premiums quoted exceeded the mortality rate statistics of those companies. Rickshaw pullers are hard-working labourers, and the premiums should be reduced as much as possible. Moreover, the Mutual Aid Association itself has considerable accumulated funds, so self-insurance is more economical and reasonable. Therefore, the Insurance Committee's self-insurance plan was also approved by the board of directors. In addition, regarding the continued registration and licensing of rickshaw pullers, once the Municipal Council makes a decision, the license fees for all new rickshaw pullers will be paid by the Mutual Aid Association.

At the beginning of this month, when the rickshaw owners stopped operating, the Mutual Aid Association's board of directors convened a special meeting and resolved to provide relief funds of 30 cents of the silver dollar to each unemployed rickshaw puller every two days during the rickshaw owners' strike period. The association immediately made every effort to prepare for the issuance of the relief funds and decided to choose three locations far from each other in the northern district as the distribution points for the relief funds. However, the rickshaw owners' strike broke down on the evening of the third day, so the relief plan was terminated.

Ningbo Bank – Recent News from the Restoration Preparatory Office – Depositors are Enthusiastic About Investing in Domestic Goods Enterprises

In accordance with the Ministry's deadline, the Ningbo Industrial Bank Restoration Preparatory Office completed the disbursement procedures for the savings section at the end of last month. The remaining funds are invested in the Shanghai Fuxing National Goods Company, which is very enthusiastic. Zhou's Civil Case Withdrawn Voluntarily

Zhang Jinxiu Realizes She Was Wrong

Zhou Wumin, a Ningbo person engaged in the insurance business, was accused by his former maid Zhang Jinxiu of offenses against morals and forgery. When the court opened the trial previously, because public attendance was prohibited, the previous reports were quite vague. It is now known that Ms. Zhang was employed as a maid in Zhou's family for more than two years. At the beginning, her service was diligent and she gained the trust of her employer. However, on the night of January 19th of this year, she secretly hid Mrs. Zhou Hu's gold necklace in her pocket. She was then searched and scolded by Mrs. Hu. Feeling ashamed, she resigned the next day. More than a month later, the woman suddenly sent a letter from a lawyer to Zhou Shimin, asking how he would deal with her impending childbirth. Zhou realized that she wanted to take the opportunity to defraud him, so he ignored her. Thereupon, Ms. Zhang filed a criminal lawsuit against Zhou in the First Special Court, and Zhou also hired a lawyer to defend himself, saying that since the plaintiff was pregnant, after she gave birth, the fetus could be examined according to law, and it would not be difficult to clarify who the child belonged to. The allegation of abandonment would also be easily resolved, and the allegation of forgery was even more groundless. Since the first trial, Ms. Zhang has been willing to reconcile. Zhou's relatives and friends were asked to mediate. As a result, Zhang Jinxiu signed an agreement with Zhou and applied to the court to withdraw the lawsuit. The declaration signed by her stated: "Zhang Jinxiu is aware that the self-sought case against Zhou Shimin is unjustified. She is willing to withdraw the self-sought part of this case and abandon all rights of appeal, and will never cause further disputes. As for the non-self-sought part of this case, Zhang Jinxiu will no longer make any claims. To have evidence for future use, this declaration is made for record." Therefore, when the court continued the trial the day before yesterday afternoon, the lawyers of both parties appeared in court to explain the reconciliation process. Judge Jiang approved the withdrawal of the self-sought case.

Song Guozhen Commits Suicide Due to Economic Hardship

Song Guozhen, a native of Suzhou, aged twenty-six, was working at Yishun and Box Making Shop in Laobeimen Nei Xuenongdi, within the city. Recently, due to economic hardship, he suddenly conceived the idea of death. Yesterday afternoon at 1:40 PM, he went to the Yong'an Hotel in the French Concession and booked room number unknown. Shortly after, he secretly swallowed raw opium and committed suicide. Later, the poison took effect and became uncontrollable. The tea boy discovered him and rushed him to Renji Hospital in a car. However, the treatment was ineffective, and he died at 6:10 PM. Before the incident, he had written a suicide note to his sister at the Xinyi Pharmacy on Route Massenet, stating that he suffered from economic pain in the world and thought it was better to die.

Private Possession of Firearms: Three-Month Sentences

Hua Youshan and Chen Dabao, Chinese detectives of the Hongkou Police Station, acting on intelligence, at 4:50 AM on the 26th of last month, discovered that someone was privately storing firearms in Room 22 of the Xi'an Hotel at No. 98 Xi'an Road, plotting illegal activities. They claimed to have been deceived and sought leniency. The court ordered them to be remanded in custody to await judgment. Shanghai Birth Control Association Invites Mrs. Martin to Speak Yesterday

Global Food Supply Can Support 5 Billion People, Half the Population Already Exists

With the Advancement of Science and Elimination of War, Birth Control is Essential

Mrs. Martin, a British expert in promoting birth control, arrived in Shanghai on the 5th of this month. Yesterday afternoon at 5:30 PM, at the invitation of the Shanghai Birth Control Association, she gave her first speech at the Shanghai Young Women's Christian Association at No. 999 Jing'an Temple Road. The topic of the speech was "Population Problems and Birth Control." Despite the rain, over a hundred Chinese and foreign men and women attended. Chairman Liu Wang Liming presided. Details are as follows:

Past Work of the Shanghai Birth Control Association

Chairman Liu Wang Liming first stood up to introduce, stating that this lecture was the first public lecture of the Shanghai Birth Control Association. The Shanghai Birth Control Association was established ten years ago. Its motivation is to create an excellent nation, establish happy families, and realize a bright society for the country. It also aims to reduce the economic burden on parents, reduce pain from diseases, and eliminate worries about having too many children. For children, it aims to provide healthy bodies, beautiful lives, and thorough nurturing. It is a great humanitarian movement. The ten years can be divided into two stages. The first half was initiated by Dr. Yan Fuqing and others, focusing on research work. Two years ago, Zhou Zhonghuiqing, who was studying birth control issues in the United States, returned to China and joined the association to assist. Therefore, the association's work has moved from the research stage to the implementation stage. Through the efforts of the association, three birth control clinics have been established: at Guangren Hospital on Avenue Edward VII, at the Women and Children's Hospital in Ximen, and at the Chinese Red Cross Hospital on Route Haig. These clinics provide consultation and guidance for those who wish to practice birth control. Also, in the past, birth control was almost exclusively enjoyed by the upper and middle classes. The association has now started to promote and guide birth control in civilian communities such as civilian new villages and rickshaw driver unions, so that it can be universally practiced. She then introduced Mrs. Martin, stating that Mrs. Martin had given 45 speeches in India, 6 in Guangdong, and many in Hong Kong. She has special research on birth control.

Speech Begins with Emphasis on Production

Mrs. Martin then began her speech, stating that the topic was "Population Problems and Birth Control." Currently, all countries in the world are paying attention to the population problem. However, some national leaders are exclusively encouraging childbirth. According to research results from British and American experts, the world can still support 5 billion people, so it seems to be a less important issue. However, no matter which country, if it cannot provide its people with a comfortable life, it should promote birth control. Encouraging childbirth should depend on the ability of the producers.

Production Should Depend on Economic Circumstances

"Birth Control" was promoted by Mrs. Sanger in the United States in 1914, as a new term, but it is actually an old problem. If we look at it from a historical perspective, couples have always been burdened by having too many children. Although there were birth control methods at the time, they were very cruel. Now, with the advancement of science, there is no problem. The meaning of birth control is not "not wanting children," but "producing according to our needs." That is, we should produce the number of children that our economic situation can support. Birth control is not abortion. Physiologically speaking, abortion is after the fetus has been formed, while birth control is before the fetus has been formed, so there is no sin.

Ideal Marriage Problems

Today, I will only talk about family population issues. Marriage is not for the purpose of having children. Young men and women want to be permanent friends because of career, love, and other factors. After marriage, having one child is very happy. The second child is also happy, but after two or three years, having another child is still pleasant, but also hard work. Year after year, the happy and beautiful girl has changed into an old mother. In our ideal marriage, young people should be examined by a doctor before marriage. This is very important because it judges whether they are qualified to be parents, just like testing soldiers for combat effectiveness in wartime. If a woman has already had a child after marriage, she will gain a lot from going to a birth control guidance center. Once guided, she can no longer fear having a second child. It can make the first child receive good nurturing. The personal care that babies receive from their mothers in the first one or two years will greatly benefit their lives. The fact that there are fewer stillborn children compared to younger siblings is proof.

Birth Control Allows Women to Rest

Physiologically and medically, women should have a period of rest after giving birth. However, those who oppose birth control say that couples should stop sexual life during this period of rest. However, according to a famous British doctor, this move would destroy the relationship between the couple, which is not as good as birth control. The number of children a family needs should be determined by economic circumstances. Some opponents say that children belong to the country and, regardless of the number, should be raised by the country. But before this social system is reformed, there are millions of children groaning in the painful life of hunger and cold.

Birth Control Can Produce Excellent Children

In the past, parents often regarded their children as private property, hoping to enjoy their support in old age. In order to promote the early realization of their dreams, they made underage children work in factories to support their families. This has attracted the attention of some countries and has been restricted. Even this concept is gradually weakening. The birth control movement is not only to control those with many children, but also to allow those without children to know how to produce excellent children through birth control guidance. In the future, the birth of children will first select their parents. If the parents are not healthy, they can refuse to produce. If the parents do not have enough food and clothing, they can also avoid it. (The master of humor, Xiao Bonan, once said, "There are gardens but no children in the east end of London, and there are children but no gardens in the west end." In the future, those with gardens can also have children.) Also, if their parents do not have the opportunity for education, they can refrain from producing children. As there are 2 million unemployed people in the UK, their children have little opportunity to be educated. Therefore, those who practice birth control must have a job before producing children. Birth control advocates are the spokespersons for children who cannot express their opinions.

Birth Control Should Be Guided by Doctors

As for the future of birth control, doctors can guide the public on birth control methods. Every medical school must include birth control knowledge in the curriculum for students to use when they practice medicine in the future. Poor people can also get free opportunities. Therefore, birth control cannot be solved by simply reading newspaper articles. It is necessary to consult hospitals. There are many birth control drugs on the market. If you buy and use them without a doctor's approval, you will not only lose money but also harm your health. I hope people in Shanghai will not be fooled. Also, those who oppose birth control often say that once the birth control movement becomes popular, morality will be extremely corrupt. But if young people have proper sex education and hygiene knowledge, they can improve their morality.

Birth Control Solves the Population Problem

If we do not practice birth control and let our descendants reproduce indefinitely, then there will be no change after a thousand years, but after a million years, the increase in number will be astounding. There is a natural population limit in the universe, such as famine, epidemics, wars, and infanticide. In the 14th century, almost half of Europe's population died of plague. In the last war, 100,000 men died on the battlefield, causing 100,000 women to lose their marriage partners and preventing the birth of tens of millions of children. Now, with the advancement of medicine, diseases and hardships are no longer a problem. The League of Nations is also seeking international peace to eliminate war. If the world is truly free of diseases and wars, then there is no other way to solve the population problem except for birth control.

Comparison of Mortality Rates Between England and India

Under the same government in England and India, the birth rate in England was similar to that in India sixty years ago, but India had a higher infant mortality rate. Both places have civil education. Now the standard of living in England has increased, and life is happier, but India is the opposite. The difference is that the British can practice birth control, while India cannot. Currently, the infant mortality rate in England is 57 per 1,000, while in India it is 200. The maternal mortality rate is 4 per 1,000 in England and 20 in India. The number of children who die young is 5 per 1,000 in England and 25 in India.

Hope for Audience's Sympathy

Finally, Mrs. Martin hoped that the audience could sympathize with her speech and promote birth control to make families happy and spread it to the general society and the country, eliminating war, and promoting it from various countries to the world, so that the world will universally grow excellent, healthy and educated citizens.

Will Be Invited to Give a Political Speech

Mrs. Martin is not only a birth control expert but also a leader in the British women's movement. She was imprisoned for participating in the suffrage movement. Therefore, the Shanghai women's community will invite her to give another political speech.

Dispute Over Buying a Copper Basin Hat

Old Goods Vendor Loses Arm

Wang Deyi Admits Temporary Mishap

Shen Xinglong, a 27-year-old man from Shandong, sells old goods in the area of ​​Minquan Road in the French Concession. On the 28th of last month, he was selling a copper basin hat on the street. Wang Deyi, a 51-year-old man from Haizhou, came forward to buy it. They agreed on a price of four foreign coins, but Wang suddenly denied it and only agreed to pay two foreign coins. So the two sides argued, and Wang acted violently. Inadvertently, he broke Shen's left arm bone. Shen cried out for help. The police arrived and arrested Wang. They took him to the police station and sent the injured man to the hospital. Yesterday, Wang was sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the Second Special Court. First, the police lawyer stated the situation and said that the police were prosecuting for serious injury. Then Shen Yilong said that the doctor diagnosed that the people's left hand had become disabled. When Wang Deyi was questioned, the man said that it was caused by a temporary mistake and asked for grace. The judge ruled to postpone the review and send the injured to the court for forensic examination to clarify the injuries before re-examination.

Sissler (transliterated), a Polish doctor, 56 years old, had a clinic at No. 121 Hankou Road, where he also lived. After a brief examination, he was taken to the Public Concession Hospital. Treatment was ineffective. He died in the morning. Yesterday morning, Tang, the prosecutor of the First Special District Court, accompanied by Wei, Zhang, and two forensic doctors, and Secretary Wang Zuyi, went to the morgue to examine the body. According to the detective's report, Tang concluded that the deceased Sissler, male, was poisoned. Sissler's wife signed for the body to be taken back for burial. The syringe was taken to the hospital for examination.

False Accusation of Car Theft, Illegal Detention, Extortion

Six Offenders Separately Punished

Qin Linfa, Zhang Guanmu, and Zhang Jinlin, who were from the same village, saw him. They said that the car was stolen and took him to Room 51 of the Hongfu Inn on Daxin Street. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi came to the Third Criminal Court to interrogate the witnesses. The six offenders were speechless and tasted the iron bars.

Rend Association Buries Exposed Corpses and Coffins

Collects More Than One Hundred in Two Days

In the wilderness of Beishi Pagoda and Paotaiwan in Wusong Town and Lijiazhai in the West City, there are many exposed corpses and coffins, all left behind by poor migrant workers. These coffins are made of thin wood and are easily broken, resulting in blood spillage and a foul odor. Corpses are dragged around by wild dogs, and bones are everywhere. Shen Yiqiu, a member of the Rend Association in the East City of Wusong, and Hou Xizhou, the director of the burial department, were greatly concerned about hygiene, especially this spring. They personally supervised the burial workers to collect more than one hundred masterless coffins from the above-mentioned locations on the previous two days when it was Qingming. They hired a boat to transport them to the Jialou Bridge Cemetery in Songxi for burial to comfort the souls and improve hygiene.

The City's Weather is Sultry and Muggy: Two Thunderstorms Yesterday; Low Pressure Has Not Receded, More Rain Expected

Since the beginning of spring, the city's climate has been cold, almost like winter. From Qingming Festival the day before yesterday, it suddenly turned warm, with temperatures rising to 82 degrees. Yesterday, due to low pressure, there was a sudden downpour at 6:00 AM, with a din of rain on the roof tiles and booming thunder. This was the first thunder of the year. It stopped after half an hour. After 9:00 AM, the sky was still normal and the sun was shining, but it was unusually hot, no less so than the day before. Unexpectedly, by 4:00 PM, dark clouds gathered again, and it suddenly became sultry again. Around 5:00 PM, a thunderclap struck, followed by a violent wind and heavy rain. After half an hour, the thunder and rain stopped again, but the temperature remained extremely muggy. Yesterday's high temperature was 81.3 degrees, and the low was 59.9 degrees. Compared with the same day last year, the high was 59 degrees and the low was 47.5 degrees, a difference of over 21 degrees. It is reported that the atmospheric pressure is still low. The report at 2:00 PM yesterday indicated two low-pressure areas: one at 33 degrees north latitude, 104 degrees east longitude, moving east; and the other at 28 degrees north latitude, 105 degrees east longitude, moving northeast by east. This low pressure is approximately downstream of Jiujiang. Therefore, based on the normal wind direction and prediction, the local area may still encounter low pressure and thunderstorms.

Li Jinhui Fails to Repay Dance Loan: Sues Guarantor Chen Xiaodie; The Lender is Hu Guigeng of Chunqiu Company; Chen Xiaodie Claims Hu Did Not Pay the Second Loan Installment

Recently, the dancer Li Jinhui, whose "Standard Beauty" Xu Lai announced her divorce from him, planned to take his Bright Moon Dance Troupe to perform in the South Seas (Nanyang) in the winter of 1934. Lacking travel expenses and costumes, he entered into a loan agreement with Hu Guigeng, the head of the Chunqiu Company in the South Seas. The company would lend Li $5,000 for costumes and $2,500 for travel expenses to help Li's trip to the South Seas. If Li earned a surplus from his performances in the South Seas, after first repaying the $7,500 loan, the company would also share a portion of the surplus. The contract was signed in November 1934, with Chen Xiaodie acting as guarantor. If Li failed to fulfill the contract, Chen would be responsible for repaying the loan. After the contract was signed and the money paid, Li has still not fulfilled the contract to this day. The company has therefore hired lawyer Qiu Hanping to file a lawsuit against Chen Xiaodie in the First Special District Court, requesting that she fulfill her responsibility to guarantee the loan. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng heard the case in the Twelfth Civil Court. Chen Xiaodie hired lawyer Zuo Deshou to defend her, arguing that the reason Li did not go to the South Seas was that the company had not paid the second installment of the $2,500 travel expenses that were due, causing the trip to fail, and that he did not intend to break the contract. Judge Huang summoned Li Jinhui for questioning and ordered the case to be continued for further investigation.

Secretary of Lawyer Jin Yu Almost Illegally Arrested: Falsely Accused in a Case, Investigation Proves No Involvement; Huang Jiande Not Handed Over to the International Settlement – Lawyer Jin Files a Protest

Huang Jiande, a native of Suzhou and a secretary at lawyer Jin Yu's office at 68 Avenue Dubail in the French Concession, is over twenty years old and extremely honest. He is especially amiable and approachable. He previously assisted the famous lawyer Wang in managing legal affairs. Later, when Wang was appointed presiding judge of the Criminal Division of the Zhenjiang Fifth Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, Huang was hired by lawyer Jin Yu as a secretary and has served to this day for almost two years. Unexpectedly, yesterday at 9:30 AM, Chen Chengkun, a Chinese detective No. 194 from the International Settlement police, went directly to lawyer Jin's office and led Huang out, telling Huang that his (Huang's) cousin Huang Dong, who works at the Lao Jie Fu silk store on Nanjing Road, had recently embezzled $40 from the store. After being arrested and questioned, Huang Dong confessed that he had borrowed the stolen money to Huang Niangyuan, so Huang Niangyuan was suspected and was ordered to be arrested and brought in for questioning. Huang was shocked to hear this. He knew that he had no cousin named Huang Dong, and even if he did, they rarely met. As for the confession that he had borrowed twenty dollars of the stolen money, that was absolutely false. Huang immediately asked the detective who had come to arrest him from the British Concession Police why he had not legally come with an officer from the French Police and refused to go with him. Detective Chen then summoned the Chinese police to the Central Police Station and called the British Concession Police to send officers to take him away. At the same time, lawyer Jin Yu, upon hearing the news, immediately went to the French Municipal Police Headquarters at the Wan Zi Ma Lu to see the police chief, stating that Detective Chen was suspected of illegal arrest and requesting that, before the case was clarified, he should first be handed over to the Second Special District Court in accordance with the law, and then the British Concession Police should formally prepare a document to take him away, which would be legal. The French police chief also believed that Detective Chen's procedures were not legal, and so together with the Zhong Lan Police Station, sent Detective Chen and Huang to the Wan Zi Ma Lu Police Station. At the same time, the Public Concession Police brought the main suspect, Huang Dong, to the French Police Station. After the French police chief questioned the suspect in detail, Huang Dong finally confessed that Huang Jiande was innocent and that all the $40 he had obtained was used to buy coats, etc. The French police chief, upon hearing the confession that Huang Jiande had no criminal suspicion, did not allow the British Concession Police to take him away, and around 5:00 PM last night, sent police to return Huang to lawyer Jin Yu. However, lawyer Jin believed that this illegal arrest needed to be remedied, and yesterday sent a letter to French Consul General Bodet and the French Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association requesting intervention.

The 277th Inspection Report on the Issuance Reserve of Central Bank Convertible Notes states: "In accordance with the provisions of Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, this committee is responsible for inspecting the amount of convertible notes issued by this bank and its reserves. The 277th inspection was held at the issuing department of this bank on April 4, 1936. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 253,733,356 silver dollars, including 230,147,435 silver dollar notes and 23,585,921 subsidiary coin notes. The total amount of convertible note reserves is 253,733,356 silver dollars, including 170,170,056 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve is deposited in the bank's issuing head office and branch warehouses and various branches, totaling 138,388,528.71 dollars, and in fellow banks, totaling 31,711,527.29 dollars. The collateral reserve is equivalent to 83,633,300 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 373,324.70 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserves is 373,324.70 yuan. This reserve includes 7,351.95 taels of bar gold, with a fixed price of 5.0779, totaling 373,324.70 yuan in customs gold. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60%, and the remainder must be secured with legal collateral. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the collateral reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This report is hereby made. April 6, 1936, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fusun, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyun."

Letter

To the Editor: I have read the news in the newspapers of the 6th that the business at No. 31-33, Yanhai Road, Liuhe Glass Factory, was careless, causing damage to the third floor of the No. 29 Minhua Umbrella Factory. I admire the fairness of your editor and the thoroughness of your reporters' investigation. However, I was surprised to read in your newspaper of the 7th a follow-up report on the fire on Yanhai Road, stating that the fire started in the third factory of Minhua. After investigation, our factory's housing has never had a stove, and the rear of the third floor is used as a kitchen. Moreover, the house is a concrete building, so there is little risk of fire. This is one point. If it is said that we were preparing food and wine to treat our workers on Qingming Festival, the fire at Liuhe was at almost 9:00 AM, and our factory had not yet finished breakfast. How could we have had time to prepare food and wine? This is the second point. Furthermore, fire rises from below, never from above. This is the third point. Therefore, I am writing to request that you correct this. To the Shen Bao, Minhua Third Factory, No. 29 Yanhai Road, April 7.
