Our Country's Radio Imports: Annual Value of 2 Million Gold Units; There are Currently 89 Radio Stations Nationwide; Shanghai Has Approximately 100,000 Radios or More

In recent years, our country's radio broadcasting industry has progressed by leaps and bounds, rapidly advancing. There are a total of 89 radio stations nationwide. In the past three years, the import of radios and parts has been approximately 2 million gold units per year. The huge leak is shocking. The details are explored and recorded as follows:

The Start of Radio Stations in Our Country

The start of radio broadcasting in our country began in 1922 when an American company founded the China Radio Company in Shanghai, broadcasting with a 50-watt radio station. However, it was discontinued shortly after due to poor sound quality. By 1924, the Carlow Company established a branch in Shanghai and set up a 100-watt radio station to broadcast Western music records. In 1927, the New New Company installed a 50-watt broadcasting station to report on business conditions and current events, and also inserted Chinese medicine and Chinese records. Subsequently, radio stations in various provinces and cities such as Tianjin, Beiping, Zhejiang, Kunming, Hankou, Nanjing, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, Nanchang Garrison Headquarters, Shandong Provincial Capital, and Hebei were established one after another. The largest of these is the Central Radio Station. In total, there are currently 89 radio broadcasting stations nationwide (excluding the four northeastern provinces), distributed in the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Shandong, Henan, Anhui, Hubei, Sichuan, Jiangxi, Fujian, Guangdong, Yunnan, and Guangxi.

Statistics on Radio Stations in Shanghai

In addition to the municipal government's radio station, almost all radio stations in this city are privately operated. The broadcast programs focus on advertising and entertainment (with two evangelical Buddhist groups promoting religion). The highest power of each station is 600 watts, and the lowest is 30 watts. The names and power ratings are recorded below: China-Thailand 45, China-America Westerner 600, Eastland 100, Overseas Chinese 500, Eastland 100, Together-Enjoy 50, Mainland 100, Jianhua 100, Zhou Xieji 75, Asia-East 100, New New 50, Dunben 100, Qikai 30, Gospel 150, Stability 50, Allied 100, Fuxing 100, Li Shude Hall 100, Mingyuan 100, Buddhist Voice 500, Oriental 100, Sino-Western 100, China-America 100, Shanghai 100, Yuanchang 50, Asia-Sound 200, Central Research 100, Greater China 100, Shipping 100, Guohua 100, Lili 100, China-Yu 100, Ministry of Communications 500, Municipal Sound 100, China-East 200, Hui-Yuan 50, New Sound 50, French 100, Her Ming 30, Its Beauty 250, China-Light 200, Municipal Government 500.

Estimates of Radios

The music broadcast by radio stations is received by radios, so the number of radios is increasing year by year. The number of radios in our country lacks reliable statistics, so the exact number is still lacking an accurate estimate. According to the latest figures released by the International Telecommunication Union's Radio Registration Office, there are a total of more than 63,000 registered radios (a portion of which were transferred to the interior after registration), but the number of unregistered radio users is very large. According to general estimates, the total number of radios in Shanghai is approximately 100,000 or more.

Japanese Goods are Imported the Most

Nineteen out of ten radios on the market are imported. Each radio costs tens of dollars at the very least and hundreds of dollars at most. The more tubes, the more expensive the price. Ordinary ones have four to seven tubes. Those with eleven or twelve tubes cannot be had for less than several hundred dollars. Profit rights flow outwards, and the leakage is very large. In the past three years, the import of radios and parts in our country has consistently hovered around 2 million gold units. Among them, American goods have seen increases and decreases, while British products have decreased year by year. German goods have increased year by year, but Japanese goods have increased the fastest. As for domestically produced radios, they are still in their infancy. Due to high costs and sluggish sales, shipments are extremely rare.

Fishing for Shrimp Turns Up a Large Bomb: Hammering it Leads to Four Deaths; Xu Shoufu and Son Blown Up on the Spot; Zhou Shuli and Brothers Die One After Another from Injuries

Xu Shoufu (48 years old, native of Jiangyin), a boatman, and his son Xu Gengsheng (24 years old) made a living by fishing for shrimp along the riverbank in the Donggou and Gaoqiao area of ​​Pudong. At noon the day before yesterday, while Xu Shoufu was fishing in the river near Chenjiazuiz in Gaoqiao, he caught a bomb, which he took ashore. He and three brothers from the village, Zhou Shuli, Zhou Shuyi, and Zhou Shuxin, inspected it. None of them recognized it as an extremely dangerous bomb, so they hammered it with an iron hammer. The bomb immediately exploded. Xu Shoufu and Xu Gengsheng, father and son, were directly hit. Both feet were blown off, their abdomens were torn open, and their intestines spilled out. They died on the spot. Zhou Shuli (28 years old), Zhou Shuyi (25 years old), and Zhou Shuxin (22 years old), who were next to them, suffered serious injuries to their heads, abdomens, hands, and feet. The Donggou Police Station was informed and sent police to the scene. Zhou Shuli died of his injuries almost immediately. The police sent Zhou Shuyi and Zhou Shuxin to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. After arriving at the hospital, Zhou Shuxin's breathing was short, and his head was swollen like a dou. He could not be saved and died. Only Zhou Shuyi's injuries were lighter, and he may be unharmed. Yesterday morning, Baochang Ling Amu reported the incident to the local court. After receiving the report, the court commissioned Prosecutor Tang Ruxiu and inspectors to first go to Shanghai Hospital to inspect the body of Zhou Shuxin, and then cross the river to Donggou to inspect the three corpses of Xu Shoufu, Xu Gengsheng, and Zhou Shuli, confirming that they had been blown to death, and ordered their families to prepare coffins separately. By the time the judge finished the inspection and returned to the court, it was dusk.

Business Report of China Insurance Co., Ltd.

From January 1, 1935, to December 31, 1935, this is the fourth year of the company's operation. The finalized accounts have been prepared into various forms. The following is a summary of the situation for your review:

Fire Insurance Business Status

The gross fire insurance premium income for this term, excluding reinsurance premiums allocated by foreign affiliated companies, amounted to 959,463.73 yuan in national currency. Compared with the previous term's gross income of 816,154.72 yuan in national currency, there is a significant increase. The net premium income, after deducting reinsurance premiums, has increased from 169,397.72 yuan in the previous term to 401,307.61 yuan in national currency this term. Paid and unpaid compensation totaled 173,751.35 yuan in national currency, accounting for 43.30% of the net premium. Operating expenses totaled 105,973.90 yuan in national currency, accounting for approximately 26.41% of the net premium. After offsetting income and expenses under commissions, the remaining amount is 66,732.36 yuan in national currency. In addition, including the interest generated from the previous term's surplus reserve, the total profit for this term's fire insurance portion is 105,938.72 yuan in national currency, while the previous term's profit was 127,158.14 yuan in national currency. Regarding the fire insurance reserve, in addition to the standard 40% allocation, an additional 80,000 yuan in national currency was allocated from the fire insurance profit to strengthen the company's financial position. Thus, the remaining balance under the fire insurance profit is 25,938.72 yuan in national currency, which is transferred to the general profit and loss account. During the spring and summer seasons of this term's operation, due to the reduction in goods stored in various regions, there were many premium refunds. Fortunately, since autumn, the trade situation has gradually improved, and the business has also become more prosperous. Therefore, the gains made at the end of the period were still significant. At the beginning of winter, the international situation became tense, and military insurance business suddenly became frequent. By the end of the year, the situation had eased, and things returned to normal.

Overview of Marine and Miscellaneous Insurance Business

The gross marine insurance premium income for this term has increased from 146,298.95 yuan in national currency in the previous term to 389,716.73 yuan in national currency this term. The net premium income, after deducting reinsurance premiums, is 60,670.64 yuan in national currency. Paid and unpaid compensation totaled 17,207.21 yuan in national currency. The scope of marine insurance business is still mainly limited to the domestic transportation of goods and raw gold and silver. Regarding the reserve, it is also allocated according to the usual practice of 20% of the net premium income.

Although automobile insurance business only accounts for a small portion of the company's overall business volume, the premium income is 11,928.98 yuan in national currency, while the compensation paid is only 3,020.09 yuan in national currency. This performance is still commendable. Several types of insurance in marine and miscellaneous insurance have very short insurance periods. Therefore, they have all expired by the end of the year, and there is no outstanding liability. As a result, there is no need to allocate reserves. The company's business scope has been expanding daily this term. For example, elevator insurance, glass insurance, and accident insurance have been launched successively. Although it is known that this type of business will develop in the future, for the convenience of customers, regardless of the variety and complexity, we accept all applications with diligence to meet the needs of our policyholders.

The profit from marine and miscellaneous insurance for this term is 36,355.00 yuan in national currency, which is a significant improvement compared to the previous term's profit of only 9,630.17 yuan in national currency. Out of this profit, 20,000 yuan in national currency is allocated to the reserve, and the remaining 16,355.00 yuan in national currency is transferred to the general profit and loss account.

Overview of Life Insurance Business

The growth and decline of life insurance business reflect the prosperity and decline of the national economy. The continued existence of usury hinders the progress of life insurance. With the gradual decline in interest rates, efforts to promote life insurance business are still essential.

The new insured amount for this term reached 1,680,224.06 yuan in national currency, compared to only 1,330,959.71 yuan in national currency in the previous term. The total amount of effective insurance as of December 31, 1935, is recorded as follows:

Ordinary Life Insurance: 2,629,496.01 yuan in national currency.

Group Life Insurance: 4,172,366.00 yuan in national currency.

The above-mentioned group life insurance is mostly short-term, and the required reserves have been adequately allocated.

The life insurance reserve for this term has increased from 100,000 yuan in national currency to 150,000 yuan in national currency, which is allocated from this term's profit. The remaining 4,266.01 yuan in national currency is transferred to the general profit and loss account.

General Profit and Loss Account

Among the company's loans, many are secured by real estate. Considering the recent decline in real estate market prices and the bleak outlook for the future market, it is necessary to allocate 80,000 yuan in national currency from this term's profit as an investment reserve, which, together with the amount allocated in the previous term, totals 130,000 yuan in national currency. However, looking at the current real estate situation, it seems to be gradually turning around. The reserves allocated by the company successively should be sufficient to cope with future changes. The market price of various domestic public bonds is actually far higher than the prices listed in the balance sheet.

The company's business is becoming increasingly complex, and the number of employees is also gradually increasing. To solve the future accommodation problem for colleagues, 20,000 yuan in national currency has been allocated from the profit as a real estate fund. It is hoped that further allocations will be made from the next term's profit to expedite the completion of the project.

The special reserve fund item listed in the company's account summary will be renamed as the general reserve in the future.

The net profit earned this term, after deducting various reserves, is 267,323.17 yuan in national currency, which is a significant increase compared to the previous term's profit of 259,273.73 yuan in national currency. After allocating 26,732.32 yuan in national currency to the public reserve from this term's profit, the remaining 240,590.85 yuan in national currency will be distributed as follows:

Dividend (annual interest rate of 6%): 150,000 yuan in national currency

Allocated to General Reserve: 90,590.85 yuan in national currency

The company's various funds are listed as follows:

Paid-up Share Capital: 2,500,000 yuan in national currency

Public Reserve: 94,282.89 yuan in national currency

General Reserve: 698,546.04 yuan in national currency

Investment Reserve: 130,000 yuan in national currency

Real Estate Fund: 20,000 yuan in national currency

Fire Insurance Reserve: 380,523.04 yuan in national currency

Marine and Miscellaneous Insurance Reserve: 89,110.82 yuan in national currency

Life Insurance Reserve: 196,794.72 yuan in national currency

Total: 4,109,257.51 yuan in national currency (End)

Shanghai Ham Sales Industry - Compiled by China Editor (A General Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce - 21)

The sole raw material for ham is pork, which is a by-product of farming. Therefore, ham production is all located inland, and Shanghai is merely a market for consumption or sales. Ham can be categorized as Southern Ham, Northern Ham, and Yunnan Ham. The quality varies, and the prices are also different. The production and sales situations are even more disparate. These will all be described separately below to provide a comprehensive overview for reference.

1. Categories of Ham and Their Production and Sales Overview

As mentioned earlier, ham can be categorized as Southern Ham, Northern Ham, and Yunnan Ham. Southern Ham is produced in Zhejiang, commonly known as Jinhua Ham. People only know that Jinhua produces ham, but they don't realize that Jinhua only produces a part of it. Other counties such as Lanxi, Dongyang, Yiwu, Yongkang, Pujiang, and Wuyi also produce ham. Among them, Dongyang's products are the most numerous, and the Jiang Ham known throughout the world is produced in that county. The bamboo ham produced in Pujiang is also quite famous, but the production volume is not large. According to general estimates, the total pork production in the above-mentioned counties is about 750,000 heads per year, of which more than two-fourths are used for ham production. The ham produced is transported through Hangzhou and Jiaxing and sold in Shanghai, accounting for the majority. The production volume of Southern Ham is less than that of Northern Ham, but in recent years, due to the larger number of people who prefer Southern Ham, the sales volume has exceeded that of Northern Ham. However, the sales volume of Southern Ham itself has also been shrinking in recent years, so its production volume has decreased from 600,000 to 700,000 pieces in the previous year to 300,000 to 400,000 pieces now. The store names and addresses of the major ham producers in each county are listed below as a reference for merchants in Shanghai to purchase goods:

Jiang Xuefang Hou Ji, Shangjiang Village, Dongyang; Jiang Xuefang Zheng Ji, Henglu, Dongyang; Da Dongyang Ham Zhuang, Chenqu, Dongyang; He Qianyuan, same as above; Jiang Jiufeng, same as above; Shao Yuantai, Chenqu, Jinhua; Xin Weihe, same as above; Huang Qianxing, same as above; Ding Longtai, Houbeili, Lanxi; Yong Shengyuan, Qianbeili, Lanxi; Zha De, same as above; Ji Wanxin, Chenqu, Yiwu; Chen Pingshun, Ximen, Yiwu; Xu Yishun, Nanguo, Yiwu; Huang Yimao, Huhua Ji, Xijie, Chenqu, Yiwu; Ding Shunchang, Yiwu; Yu Da, Chenqu, Wuyi. (To be continued)

Education News

Ministry of Education Issues - Revised Standards for High School Civics Curriculum

The Ministry of Education issued a notice to the Education Departments of all provinces and cities on June 6, stating that the table of teaching subjects for primary and high schools and the number of teaching hours per week for each subject in each semester has been revised and announced by the Ministry in February of this year, and has been distributed to the Education Departments of all provinces and cities for their records. Now, based on the revised table of teaching hours, the content of the curriculum standards for middle school subjects has been slightly improved to promote progress. The revised standards that have been completed include the curriculum standards for civics, physical education, mathematics, geography in junior and senior high schools, and physiology and hygiene in junior high schools. In addition to being announced by the Ministry, two copies of each of the revised standards are enclosed for distribution to all subordinate schools for their information. This order is accompanied by two copies of the revised curriculum standards for civics, physical education, mathematics, geography in junior and senior high schools, and physiology and hygiene in junior high schools.

Revision of Senior High School Civics Curriculum Standards

First, Objectives:

(1) To enable students to acquire the knowledge necessary for social life, as well as organizational skills and methods of handling affairs, in preparation for serving society. (2) To enable students to understand the ideology, political program, and policies of the Chinese Nationalist Party (Kuomintang) as the only path to national construction and solving social problems. (3) To enable students to understand the meaning of life, stimulate their self-awareness, establish their worldview, and cultivate their sense of current responsibility for national revival.

Second, Time Allocation:

Two hours per week per semester in the first academic year; two hours per week per semester in the second and third academic years; one hour per week per semester in the first semester of the second and third academic years.

Third, Teaching Material Outline:

(1) First Academic Year, First Semester: Social Problems, Political Overview. Social Problems: Population Problems: 1. Introduction to Population; 2. Population Problems in Our Country. Rural Problems: 1. Rural Economy; 2. Problems of Rural Decline and Revival in China. Labor Problems: 1. Labor and Production; 2. Labor-Management Cooperation; 3. Labor Problems in China. Vocational Problems: 1. Vocational Training; 2. Career Choices; 3. Professional Ethics; 4. Unemployment Relief. Marriage Problems: 1. The Social Significance of Marriage; 2. Engagement, Marriage, and Divorce; 3. Rights and Obligations between Spouses. Political Systems: 1. Democracy; 2. Dictatorship; 3. The Current Political System in Our Country. Constitutions: 1. The Meaning and Types of Constitutions; 2. The Content of Constitutions (Emphasis on the Five-Power Constitution); 3. The Creation and Amendment of Constitutions. International Relations and International Organizations: 1. Nations and International Organizations; 2. The Relationship between International Conferences and International Organizations.

(2) First Academic Year, Second Semester: Economic Overview. The Characteristics of China's Economic Society: 1. Natural Environment; 2. Cultural Background. China's Agriculture: 1. Farmland and Agricultural Products; 2. Agricultural Technology and Organization; 3. Agricultural Economy; 4. Essentials of China's Current Land Law. China's Industry: 1. Types of Industry; 2. Industrial Technology and Organization; 3. Industrial Raw Materials; 4. Industrial Investment and Management. China's Commerce: 1. Value and Price; 2. Markets and Transportation; 3. Commercial Organizations; 4. Commercial Finance; 5. International Trade and Tariffs. China's Finance: 1. The Evolution of the Financial System; 2. The Organization and Operations of Financial Institutions; 3. Discussions on Monetary Revolution and Monetary Reform. China's Public Finance: 1. Budgets and Final Accounts; 2. Public Expenditures and Revenues; 3. Public Debt; 4. Budgeting and Auditing. The Transformation of China's Economy: 1. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Industrial Plan; 2. The National Economic Construction Movement; 3. The Cooperative Movement; 4. Planned Economy.

(3) Second Academic Year, First and Second Semesters:

Essentials of Law. The Meaning and Types of Law. Various Materials Composing Law. Subjects and Objects of Rights: 1. The Meaning and Types of Rights; 2. Natural Persons and Legal Persons; 3. Property and Property Rights. Legal Acts. Obligations: 1. The Occurrence of Obligations; 2. The Extinguishment of Obligations; 3. Types of Obligations. Property Inheritance and Wills. Criminal Sanctions and Prisons: 1. The Meaning of Crime and Its Causes; 2. Criminal Trials; 3. The Functions of Prisons and the Reform of Chinese Prisons. Litigation Procedures: 1. The Organization of the Courts; 2. Civil Litigation; 3. Criminal Litigation; 4. The Lawyer System; 5. Administrative Litigation; 6. Consular Jurisdiction. (4) Third Academic Year, First Semester:

(4) Third Academic Year, First Semester:

Essentials of Ethics. The Meaning of Ethics. The Characteristics of Chinese Ethical Thought. The Characteristics of Western Ethical Thought. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Ethical Thought. The Responsibilities and Obligations of Chinese Youth. Chinese Citizens and National Revival. Note: When compiling textbooks, more concrete materials related to practical problems should be adopted, and empty discussions should be avoided. Fourth, Overview of Implementation Methods:

(1) Operational Requirements:

Student self-governing bodies and organizations such as school stores or cooperatives should be guided by the school to carry out civic training in practice. Various social organizations (including political, legal, economic, and agricultural, industrial, and commercial organizations) should be visited by students within a possible scope to obtain practical social life verification from civic education in the classroom to develop their ability to inspect and judge. The school should equip itself with good social science and youth self-cultivation books suitable for senior high school students to read about civic education, and should hold lectures, research, and other gatherings on civic education topics. Cultivate special teaching materials (such as various social relief issues, social finance regulation, and industrial and commercial management) during special periods.

(2) Teaching Essentials:

For the sake of correctly guiding youth thoughts, the content of teaching should adopt fair theories as narrative and explanatory compilations. The school environment should have appropriate arrangements and equipment for ordinary and special training to make teaching obtain full efficiency. Teachers should examine students' personalities and guide them to read good social science and youth self-cultivation books that they like to satisfy their interests and guide their thoughts well. When explaining teaching materials, attention should be paid to actual social survey materials and facts. (End)

Jiaotong University to Hold 40th Anniversary Commemoration Today

Jiaotong University of this port was founded in the twenty-second year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, and has been forty years to this day. Today (the 8th) is the fortieth anniversary of the school's establishment. Due to the seriousness of the national crisis, the school will not engage in extravagant activities, but will only hold a commemorative ceremony this afternoon. At the same time, the school's alumni association will hold its annual meeting at the school on the evening of the 11th to celebrate the anniversary of the alma mater. All programs have been drafted by the program group of the Fortieth Anniversary Commemoration Preparation Committee to facilitate the participation of the majority of alumni. In addition to the two days of suspension of classes today and tomorrow, the remaining programs do not conflict with student class time. Classes will resume as usual from the day after tomorrow (the 10th) and there will be no holiday. The school's commemorative program is excerpted below: April 7th (Tuesday) 7:00 PM Play (Gymnasium), 7:00 PM Movie (Wenzhi Hall), April 8th (Wednesday) 10:00 AM Planting Commemorative Trees, 10:00 AM Achievement Exhibition, Noon Luncheon for Old Faculty and Staff, 2:00 PM 40th Anniversary Ceremony, 4:00 PM Soccer Game, 4:30 PM Tea Party (Rong Hong Hall), 6:00 PM to 10:00 PM Celebration Conference (Gymnasium), April 9th (Thursday) 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM Welcome Visiting Groups, 10:00 AM Girls' Volleyball Game, Noon Luncheon for Phi Society, 2:00 PM National Arts, 4:00 PM Boys' Volleyball Game, 7:00 PM Movie (Wenzhi Hall), April 10th (Friday) 6:30 PM Basketball Game (Gymnasium), 7:30 PM Joint Academic Lecture by the School's Engineering Society, Management Society, and Science Society (Engineering Hall), April 11th (Saturday) 6:00 PM Alumni Association Annual Meeting. Also, President Li, in this week's commemoration of the alma mater, specially invited Dr. Ferguson, the first director of the school, Master Tang Wenzhi, the longest-serving president, and Pan Gongzhan, the director of the city's education bureau, to give speeches at the school on Monday morning. All three hoped that all teachers and students could save the times and the country with their personal character and spirit. Dr. Ferguson also said that it was fortunate to have three generations in the same hall, with himself representing the founding period of the school, Grand Master Tang representing the restoration period, and President Li representing the emerging period. The audience applauded and laughed. President Li then reported that, at a time when the country was in difficulty and the treasury was stretched thin, a large-scale celebration was not permitted by the General Political Department due to the environment. For the sake of establishing a long-term foundation for the school and planning for a century, he had sent letters to alumni in various places, requesting donations for scholarships as a permanent memorial.

Municipal Education Association Holds Citywide Elementary School Student Calligraphy Competition Final Round Scheduled for the 19th of this month. Preliminary rounds in all districts have been completed

In order to arouse the interest of elementary school students throughout the city in calligraphy, the Shanghai Municipal Education Association has specially organized a citywide elementary school student calligraphy competition, divided into preliminary and final rounds. The preliminary rounds have been completed by the education associations of each district. The final round is scheduled to be held at Junyi Middle School at 2:00 PM on the 19th of this month. Ma Gongyu, Tong Xingbai, and Li Xiaobai have been invited as judges. The judging standards are: structure 50%, ink usage 25%, and brushwork 25%. The competition items are divided into large and small regular scripts. The number of characters and the words used will be temporarily announced by the Municipal Education Association at the final. The paper will be provided by the association, and the brushes and ink will be provided by the contestants themselves. The time limit is one hour.

Tea Cocoon Lending After Qingming Festival

This spring, the weather has been cold for a long time, and the development of tea silkworms has been relatively late. Now it is after the Qingming Festival, so they have only begun to revive in the past few days. However, foreign banks' sales appetite is sluggish and financial turnover is difficult. There are not many operators this year. As far as the reporter knows, this time, the silver and money industry's lending to tea merchants, in addition to the old accounts being opened as usual, new accounts have always been politely refused. Therefore, at the time of registration, it was found that the total amount of tea loans released as of yesterday was less than one million. Compared with last year, the ratio is only one to ten. As for cocoon merchants, the silver and money industry is not only cautious in lending, but also requires favor in pledging, and the amount is not willing to be too large. In previous years, 100,000 or 200,000 was not uncommon, but now 5,000 or 10,000 is not easy.

Mixed Sentiment and a Wait-and-See Approach in Government Bonds, Minimal Sporadic Trading, Market Close Shows Slight Firmness

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange saw a market situation that, while still fluctuating, showed a slightly firmer trend. However, trading activity continued to decline, and the market remained sluggish. Both bulls and bears with significant holdings adopted a wait-and-see attitude. Although each side had its expectations, there seemed to be no clear way forward. The scope of activity was too limited, and any slight movement would inevitably cause changes, leading to self-inflicted troubles. The result of this mutual observation and persistence would inevitably cause the market price to become stagnant again, possibly only fluctuating when settlement approached. Yesterday morning, the sudden sale of E-type bonds at the opening caused the market price to weaken again, but the fluctuations remained minimal. In the second session, sporadic trading showed slightly more buying, pushing the price back up by five fen or one jiao. The oscillating situation was difficult to break. At the afternoon opening, there was a slight demand for 20-series bonds. On this small-scale stage, the price was slightly raised by about one jiao. At the close, both 20-series and 47-series bonds were being bought. Although the quantity was limited, the scarcity of sellers was even more pronounced, so the market continued to show firmness. D-type bonds rose by three jiao. The overall situation showed no new changes, and the dull, brewing atmosphere was difficult to break out of for the time being. As a result, most market prices slightly rebounded, showing gains of five fen or one jiao to three jiao and a half. The total turnover was 1,415,000 yuan, a decrease of 500,000 yuan compared to the previous day. US Cotton Still Seems Stable

Yesterday, US cotton opened with a fall of one to four points in all months. The foreign news was not good, but because industry peers, Liverpool, the mainland, and the Far East unanimously bought in, the market still seemed stable. Regarding the borrowing and defrauding of cotton, people's hearts were mixed. Near months were weak due to fears of short selling, bull liquidation, and southern selling. Liverpool buyers made some hedging purchases. New cotton was damaged in the east due to excessive rain, while the west lacked rain and was in great need. As a result, spot prices fell by four points, and futures prices rose and fell by four to six points. According to rumors from the cotton exchange, cotton hoarders sold 82,000 bales of spot cotton last week, with 234,000 bales still unsold. It is also estimated that the world's total cotton inventory as of the end of the 2nd totaled 23,363,000 bales, of which US cotton accounted for 12,278,000 bales, compared to 20,207,000 bales last year and 10,717,000 bales the year before. In addition, according to a survey by the New Orleans Exchange, as of the end of March, nine provinces had sold a total of 2,125,000 tons of fertilizer in eight months, compared to 2,225,000 tons last year. British spot cotton fell by five points, and futures fell by 34 points. The Indian cotton market was bleak, and prices softened due to the impact of US cotton loans, with Pingore falling by 1 to 1.25 rupees, Omra falling by 1.75 rupees, and White Rossi falling by 1.75 to 2.25 rupees. The original telegram is recorded on the left (telegram of the 6th).

Grains: Flour and Wheat Both Weak Yesterday

The flour market was originally bearish, but the northern gangs were buying in the market. Although it was a mental act rather than a practical stomach, people's hearts were slightly stable. The market prices of all months were close to the closing price of the previous day. By the afternoon, the warm weather was beneficial to the new wheat harvest, and the inland gangs and factories sold out, and the non-industry hoarders also followed suit, allowing for the offering of new wheat flour in the distant months, and the wheat was more flat and soft.

After the opening of the wheat market in the morning, the inland gangs and peddlers intended to sell, because the weather was gradually warming, and the wheat harvest was hopeful. The non-industry hoarders also did not rely on the goal of hoping for a good harvest. A part of the bulls immediately followed the market. There were fewer entries than exits, and transactions were deserted. The selling wind was even stronger in the afternoon, and the flour market was weak, and the market became more uneasy. Although the foreign wheat reported gains, the orders were already uneconomical, and all parties in the market did not pay attention to this. Therefore, the market continued to decline. The existing wheat is in a standing position due to the lack of goods. Yesterday, Fuxin went to the car to sell 1,400 packages of wheat, and the price was still opened at 5.32 yuan.

The drought in the United States for wheat has not been slightly reduced, and the shorts have been replenished. In addition, the morning outlook is quite good. Anhui Tea Research (II)

-- Shi Jifa

Chuzhou, Quanjiao, and Lai'an Counties: Also belong to northern Anhui, and produce a lot of tea. For example, the tea produced in Quanjiao is called Nan Qiao Tea and Bei Qiao Tea, which are mostly drunk by people in Hankou, but less so in Beijing and Shanghai. Lai'an produces Xinchang Tea, also known as Shouyang Tea, which has a fragrant aroma and a strong taste. You can't stop drinking it, and the price is relatively low. Anhui produces a lot of tea, ranking first in the country. In addition to the above-mentioned counties, Qiupu in southern Anhui, Jingxian, Taiping, Tonglu, Shitai, Xuancheng, Ningguo, Langxi, Guangde, and other counties. Taihu, Susong, Tongcheng, Lingbi, and other counties in northern Anhui also produce tea. In addition to providing for local use, there are also small vendors who transport it to neighboring provinces for sale.

Types

The types of tea produced in various tea-producing counties in Anhui are different. The findings of the survey are described as follows:

Qimen: The entire county has winding mountains and high terrain, making it a natural tea-producing area. It is considered the best and most abundant tea in the entire Huizhou. Residents of the entire county rely on tea as their only production. Residents have rich experience and research on tea tree cultivation methods. The Anhui Model Tea Plantation once tested the tea varieties of various villages in Qimen, and the result was that the Qimen Xixiang tea variety (round with one flat side, with thick grains and shells) was characteristic, and was superior to Jiangxi, Fujian, Hunan, Hubei, Zhejiang and other provinces. Naxiang tea varieties (round and triangular, with small grains and thin shells), Dongxiang and Chengxiang tea varieties (mostly round, with occasional triangular grains, small grains and thin shells) are also good.

Wuyuan: Wuyuan Fuyuan is quite wide, with many mountains and producing areas divided into Dongxiang, Ximen, and Beimen three areas, with Dongxiang producing the most, followed by Beimen and Ximen. Most of them produce green tea, and the Pearl Tea produced in Qianggong Mountain is the most excellent.

Xiuning: The production volume is the largest in the north and two districts. The tea in Naxiang has long been welcomed by foreigners. The Qimai in Baiyun Mountain, Song Mountain, and Jinlong Mountain in Beixiang are strong, and the products include Sparrow Tongue, Lotus Heart, and Jin Ya.

County: There are many producing areas in the whole county, and the most abundant one is Dazhouyuan. The baked green tea and fried green tea produced are the best in the whole 歙. If the old bamboo tea produced in Laozhu Ridge. Huangshan is entrenched in the territory, and the Tiandu Yunwu and other teas produced are extremely famous. In addition, Songzhu Mountain is also excellent, and the tea produced in Zixia Mountain is better than orchids in color, fragrance and Qing Dynasty, and is a rare treasure.

Gang County: Gangjing is narrow and mostly stone mountains, so there is less tea production. Its Zhoujiayuan tea variety is half round and half arc triangular, which is also a good variety.

Xuxi: The only producing area is the Badu in Xixiang, such as Huangzhu Mountain, Shangjin Mountain, Tea Farm, and Muyun Mountain. The production volume is large and the quality is excellent. The Shiyu tea produced in Jinshan is famous throughout the country, and the sales in North China are huge.

Huoshan: The whole territory produces tea, which is better than Lu'an. Because of its affiliation, it is covered by the name Lu'an. The mountains in the territory are high and foggy, and the Qing Dynasty Shu Qi is produced, which does not need artificial planting. Its Qing Dynasty is so unique that it cannot be added. The teas produced in the whole county include Zhulan, Jasmine, Silver Needle, Sparrow Tongue, Plum Piece, Orchid Head, Songluochun, Yuqian, Maojian, etc., which are sold to northern Anhui, Shandong, Henan, Hebei, Pingjin. The area around Shanxi is huge. The tea species are mostly multi-angled and small in size.

Lu'an: The whole territory is mountainous and produces a lot of tea. The tea produced in Songzhu Mountain has a fragrant and beautiful taste, and other mountains are decisive. The tender buds picked at the beginning are Baihao Yinzhen Sparrow Tongue, etc. Then the tender leaves are picked as plum slices, chrysanthemum cakes, etc. When it comes to the beginning of summer, the tender branches are picked and named Fen Needle.

Guangde: Belonging to southern Anhui, it also produces tea. The tea seeds are mostly three-sided round and one-sided flat, with thin shells.

Shenbao National Products Weekly

Contribution

The Hope of National Products Industry Under the Policy

— Yang An

The survival of national products lies in the national confidentiality policy, firmly establishing the national tariff barrier, and increasing the price of foreign goods to benefit the national products manufacturers, so that the national products can compete with foreign goods. If the protection policy cannot be implemented, coupled with the tax evasion and smuggling of foreign goods, which cannot be prevented, not only will national products be defeated by foreign goods, but the national economy and national finance will also be seriously affected. Mr. Bai Chongxi once said to the Liangguang Industrial Investigation Group: "If the national products industry is not protected by policies, it will be supported by hard work and suffer from difficulties and dangers. As a result, it will inevitably become a victim of imperialism." The words are sincere and chilling. We feel that the current national products industry is indeed at its extreme difficulty. The competition of peers and the dumping of foreign goods have been eroding the nascent industry every day, and the heavy burden of donations and taxes, the difficulties of transportation, and the lack of unification of the monetary system and exchange rates are all fatal injuries to industrial progress. It is true that they are each governing themselves and not seeking each other, and in the middle, they lose a lot of spiritual wealth and unnecessary expenses, which is even more uneconomical. When we investigated the national products industry in Guangdong, we threatened that the industry of a country did not have a whole plan and a way to communicate with each other? Such an uneconomical phenomenon will occur. For example, Guangdong does not produce cotton or wool. Then, instead of running a cotton weaving wool industry in Guangdong, it is better to run another industry, which is more effective and easier to achieve results. All in all, whether internally or externally, there must be policies and a whole plan, and the national products industry will have the hope of survival and long-term development.

Jinpu Machine Factory Gong Xinglei Invents National Products Dual-Purpose Folding Umbrella

— Yilu

Completed in Seven Years, the Ministry of Industry Approved Patent, Dual-Purpose for Sunny and Rainy Days, Currently Planning to Set Up a Factory for Manufacturing

Although the citizens' use of national products only started recently, in these short three months, there have been several satisfactory things, which seems to be worth our gratification.

What are these things? The first is this year's January surplus, although February was again a deficit. But if we work hard and move forward, then the word surplus seems to have the possibility of being found in the newspaper. But this is not within the scope of this article, so let's leave it alone for now. The second thing that satisfies us is that the newly invented national products continue to appear, like the national products dual-purpose folding umbrella discussed in this article, which is one of them.

Failure is the mother of success, this sentence is indeed correct. The success of the national products dual-purpose folding umbrella has gone through several failures, but what is the result? Finally achieved the purpose of success! The inventor of this kind of sunny and rainy umbrella is Mr. Sheng Jun Xinglei, who entered Hangzhou County, Zhejiang Province, is only twenty-five years old now, and has only received primary school education, but because his temperament is very suitable for engineering, he usually likes to study practical tools. In 1928, he was only seventeen years old. After graduating from primary school, he was introduced by someone to work as a toolman in the Puzhen Machine Factory of the Jinpu Railway. In his spare time, he read various books and newspapers. In 1930, he suddenly received an hint, preparing to manufacture a pocket umbrella that could be used for both sunny and rainy days. Since he made this aspiration, he has been studying all the time, day and night. At that time, many people ridiculed him, but he never moved. After studying like this for two years, the first part was successful! But when applying for a patent, the Ministry of Industry did not approve it because the manufacturing was not refined. So he made a second step of research, spending four years, and applied again for the Ministry of Industry to approve the patent, but because the use was not flexible, he was ordered to study and improve it again. Until last year, it was all completed, and the previous drawbacks of inflexible use were also gone. So the Ministry of Industry approved the patent. Although it took more than seven years, the result was very satisfactory.

The manufacturing materials of this umbrella are all national products. The external form is almost the same as a flashlight, nine inches long, one inch in diameter. When folded, it can be hidden in the pocket. The method of use is: first hold the umbrella's sliding ring and push it upwards, then use another hand to pull out the umbrella handle retracted inside, and after opening it, it is the same as an ordinary umbrella. Moreover, this umbrella can be used not only on sunny days; but also on rainy days, so it is called a dual-purpose folding umbrella for sunny and rainy days. It is also called a dual-purpose pocket umbrella for sunny and rainy days. As for when you want to shrink it, you also first hold the umbrella's sliding ring, then grab the umbrella handle with the other hand, turn one hand to the left; turn the other hand to the right; then the umbrella's sliding ring is tightened downwards, and the umbrella handle retracts upwards, and it returns to the size of a flashlight!

Since Gong Xinglei obtained the patent approval from the Ministry of Industry, he is now preparing to raise funds to set up a factory for manufacturing. If it proceeds smoothly, in the near future, this kind of dual-purpose umbrella for sunny and rainy days will be found on the market! And the price will not be very expensive, almost everyone can afford it!

Planting Tung Trees and Broadly Planting Other Oil Seedlings

— Zi

In the domestic goods special issue of the Shen Bao on the 12th of this month, Mr. Qiulang's article "During the Peak Tung Oil Export Period, Chinese People Should Quickly Plan to Plant Tung Trees" was published. The argument was insightful, and the guidance was detailed. Given the urgency of the world's needs today and the abundant profits from planting tung trees, coupled with government promotion and encouragement, and the determination of the Chinese people to improve, in a few years, the quantity and quality will increase, and exports will surge. This is indeed the only major path to promote domestic products and recover rights and interests. After reading it, I was filled with admiration. However, planting tung trees is an urgent task, and broadly planting other various oil seedlings is an even more urgent matter. The reason for the sharp increase in tung oil exports this year is due, firstly, to the urgent needs of various countries in military and scientific fields, and secondly, to the fact that the tung trees planted in the United States have not yet reached the harvest period. Therefore, it is not necessarily certain that my country's tung oil exports can maintain their advantage in a few years. Therefore, for the sake of the entire national economy, we must, on the one hand, promote the export of domestic products, and on the other hand, reduce the import of foreign goods. Currently, observing the import of foreign goods, kerosene alone accounts for more than 12 million yuan each year, which is shocking! Upon investigation, kerosene is almost entirely used for lighting. The ancients said, "A lamp like a bean," and "Accompanied by a green lamp," referring to the unimproved vegetable oil lamps of the past, whose brightness was indeed inferior to the foreign lamps that now cover the country. Therefore, the sales of kerosene are becoming increasingly prosperous, and the huge leak cannot be offset by the number of tung oil exports from my country. Now my country has invented vegetable oil lamps (invented by Zhong Ling), whose structure is based on scientific principles, providing bright light comparable to foreign lamps, while being safer, more hygienic, and saving oil. The China Oil Lamp Company (No. 218 Shandong Road, this city) manufactures and sells them, and all kinds of vegetable oils in our country can be burned. Therefore, if the Chinese people can widely plant oil seedlings, sufficient fuel can be provided, and its effect can reduce kerosene imports, which is the same goal as promoting tung oil exports. As for when international wars break out and the source of kerosene is cut off, this will be a sharp weapon for national defense. It is hoped that the entire country, from top to bottom, will pay attention, use wasteland, and widely plant oil seedlings, either to promote them abroad or to use them domestically, increasing exports on the one hand and reducing import surpluses on the other, which is a crucial plan for saving the country. After reading the article "Strive to Plant Tung Trees," I had these associations and asked the readers what they thought.

Worsted Wool Reunites the Lotus Flower

— Meng Zhao

—A tragicomedy of separation and reunion of a domestic goods couple

"Dr. Tai Shuangqiu, a practitioner of using domestic goods, is known to everyone as one of the most vigorous promoters of the domestic goods movement!" The unveiling of "Domestic Goods First Year" and the establishment of the Nianer Movement Society are well-known facts!

Anecdotes of General Göring

— Yu Translation

"Have you heard about the new cigarette cards? A set of 'Göring in Full Military Uniform'. One hundred cards—each different." This is the latest gossip material that Germans are secretly talking about.

General Göring is the German Air Force Minister and Prussian Prime Minister, who loves to wear beautiful military uniforms and hang brilliant medals. In recent months, several amusing anecdotes have occurred in Germany about him, the most popular of which is the bathroom flood.

One day, he was taking a bath at home, and the bathroom was full of water. His male servant ran to the general to report: "Master, the floor in the bathroom is already six inches deep!" "Well, I know, don't stand here talking too much, don't open your mouth," General Göring was probably a little annoyed, and suddenly shouted loudly: "Bring me my Air Force General's uniform!"

When the male servant brought the uniform, he couldn't find the general's medals and badges. He searched everywhere, but there was still no trace. Finally, when he was almost completely desperate, he suddenly remembered where the medals and badges were. It turned out that he had forgotten to take the medals and badges off his master's pajamas that morning.

As for praising this Prussian Prime Minister, which contains a joking meaning, there are really too many to enumerate. The most meaningful and interesting thing is that he received a photo album as a congratulatory gift when he got married last year. The photo album was not filled with photos, but with anecdotes about him, published in newspapers, a large amount of material collected and clipped. It is said that the Führer Hitler often talked to him about this strange gift, and laughed heartily.

Popular Songs and Mountain Songs

— Hua Ling

In the air of the city, all day long, the sound waves of songs like Little Peach Red and lyrics like Fengyang songs are broadcast from the radio, without a moment of silence, making people dizzy and wishing they could grow wings and fly to my hometown in the countryside. Because in my hometown with mountains and rivers, farmers and village women, and even girls, can all sing mountain songs that are popular and easy to understand, and have profound meaning. Although these mountain songs have not been composed by composers with staff notation, and naturally there is no violin accompaniment, they are sung leisurely and gracefully in the open air of the countryside, and the melody is so sweet that it is captivating, which cannot be described in words, and cannot be understood without experiencing it personally. Although the mountain songs in my hometown rarely contain gorgeous and seductive sentences, it is a kind of natural sound, absolutely unlike the songs popular in the city, which are completely contrived and boring because the lyrics are adapted to the melody. The author grew up in the countryside, so he has a considerable understanding and love for the mountain songs in the village. Therefore, even though I am now living in the city, whenever I wake up in the middle of the night and hear the sound of bustling music from the neighbor's radio, I always mutter, "How annoying, who wants to listen to this tune? The mountain songs in my hometown are beautiful."

A Bomb That Can Explode

—

But this time, I was disappointed. When I returned to my hometown, I didn't hear a single familiar mountain song that I used to hear in my childhood. On the ship connecting the trading port and my hometown, I heard the boatmen humming the tune of "Everyone together..." instead of the old "A girl by the river..." Along the way, I heard pedestrians on the shore humming "Gently cast the net, pull the rope tightly..." and "Thousands of peach blossoms..." each once. Rushing home, my sister-in-law was humming "Baby wants to sleep..." to coax the child to sleep. The children outside the house were singing in unison "Since Emperor Zhu came out..." It is said that mountain songs like "The moon hides in the clouds like it's shy, a young girl marries west of the stone bridge..." are no longer sung. So I couldn't help but sigh and say, "Alas, has this also invaded the countryside?"

Swapping Nesting Phoenixes

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Prologue: Appreciating Chrysanthemums Near Double Ninth Festival, Seeking Tranquil Small Gathering, Remembering Old Dreams, Drinking Hate for a Thousand Years

Because when I was a child, I met a teacher who had a red face, big cheeks, pockmarks, and a white beard. When he spoke, his saliva splashed everywhere, and his hands and feet danced, which was a bit funny. He liked to tell stories, especially love stories, we were more than Ruan Dahuzi who made swallow notes. I thought about it in my heart, and couldn't help but laugh. Lan Chang was about to ask me why I laughed, but heard a woman's voice asking: Is Mr. Lan Chang at home? Although this is a common sentence, it has a lot of Nanjing accent. This Nanjing accent is the easiest to recognize. It was unexpected that a female guest from Nanjing would visit here. So I looked towards the door, and a female guest walked over through the shade of the trees. From a distance, I saw that she was also wearing a light gray long jacket, and her figure was also very thin. Lan Chang had already rushed forward to greet her and led her in. Closer, I saw clearly that it was an old lady in her fifties. She didn't cut her hair and wore a small bun. There were a few silver strands on her round bun, which showed that she could not hide her old age. However, her face, in its thinness, had no wrinkles. On her slightly high nose, she wore a pair of old-fashioned toric glasses, half hiding her sharp eyes. She carried a large leather bag and walked slowly over to the small pavilion. Lan Chang waved to me and said: This is Mr. Ruan, brother, come and meet him. When I heard this, I felt like I had walked into a pine forest full of rough branches, and suddenly encountered a plum blossom tree. I was both surprised and happy. After Lan Chang introduced Mr. Ruan, he bowed to me and said with a smile: I have long admired you, sir. I should have visited you in , but because of my humble background, I didn't dare to make a decision. I was very happy to hear that you could come to Suzhou. Lan Chang asked Mr. Ruan to sit down, and after I said a few words of humility, I asked: Does Mr. Ruan also live in Suzhou? He smiled and said: No! Suzhou is where blessed people live, how can I live here? I asked: Do you live in Nanjing then? He smiled, and then said: I take the world as my home. I understood that he was unwilling to show his true identity. It is impolite to ask a woman about her whereabouts, no matter how old she is. So I silently sat aside and didn't interrupt for the time being. Lan Chang's house has another group of female guests, and after Mr. Ruan sat in the pavilion for a while, he led her to the inner room. I propped my head with my hand and thought for a while, thinking that his big leather bag contained a history of hardship. But I don't know how he will tell me? And how will I ask him if I don't understand something? As I was thinking this, Fang Dabai, who was sitting beside me, said to me: What are you thinking about? Do you think Mr. Ruan is strange? (6)

Notes on What I Saw

— (Hua Jia)

It's not the first time, it happens almost often, on Shangma Road, on Nanjing Road, on Sichuan Road, sometimes also on Henan Road or Shandong Road. A middle-aged man wearing a very old long robe, with a wide face, but everything seems sluggish, a round head, without dense hair, a very slow person, he always holds unusual envelopes, sometimes also smoking a cigarette, walking very slowly. As long as I get close to him, he puts the envelope in front of me, and often says in his mouth:

"Young master, young master, do you know where Yangshupu is?"

The first time he asked me, I gave him directions, telling him to go out and take the Route 8 tram to Yangshupu Road. After thanking him, he walked away again, but instead of following the directions I gave him, he walked in the opposite direction.

Later, I followed him, and he asked the second passerby again, still asking the same question. Perhaps this passerby was too busy and ignored him. After a while, he asked the third person again. This time, the passerby probably often encountered him asking people like this, and walked away without stopping. I was wondering in my heart: Why does he always ask? And why doesn't he follow the directions after asking? This strange psychology has not been resolved until now. Because since the first time, I have often seen him asking like this, and the number of times he has asked me is probably more than ten times.

Now I still don't understand, I think he is definitely not asking for directions, or "Yangshupu" and him have had something "unresolvable", so he has become so madly walking on the road asking for directions all day long. But why is he so free? Doesn't he have anything else to do all day long? Won't he have a moment of awakening?

Teaching Whip

— Shen Xigang

A teaching whip is originally a convenient teaching aid. When teachers teach in the classroom, they often use a small bamboo pole to point to the white characters on the blackboard, so that students standing on the side can easily see the characters on the blackboard without being obscured by lines.

In addition, teaching whips are used for rhythm in music lessons and to assist posture when speaking. Some are even used to whip students.

I remember when I was studying in primary school, our teacher always brought a smooth teaching whip to class. It was made of a small purple bamboo, and the outside was tightly wrapped with a light yellow head rope. Whenever we sat tired and made some noise, he would always "clap, clap" on the podium a couple of times. The students' voices disappeared. Then he could continue teaching in peace. It was a coincidence that one time, a student in the first grade fell asleep during class. He didn't know why he was particularly annoyed, so he used the teaching whip to strike the podium heavily a few times, scaring the student so much that he jumped up and finally cried and went back to tell his mother. And that night, he had a fever and chills. The next day, his mother came to school to question our teacher. As a result, our teacher expressed his deep apologies and invited a doctor to treat his student, which cost some medical expenses.

Perhaps he was stimulated by this incident. From then on, when he came to class, he lacked a smooth and light yellow teaching whip.

This was twenty years ago. Now I am also a primary school teacher myself. Whenever I see my colleagues using teaching whips in class, I think of my teacher's story twenty years ago.

Common Sense

Effective Prescriptions for Family Use

— Ai Mei

As the saying goes: "A simple prescription can make a famous doctor die of anger." In fact, there are many diseases that require time to be diagnosed and treated by a doctor, but the prescriptions passed down by the world only mention one or two things that doctors consider insignificant, and they often get better immediately after taking them. Some even have things that are beyond imagination and cannot be explained by common sense. How strange! Yang Xiangchi from Yunnan showed me a bundle of proven prescriptions: all are simple, easy to prepare, inexpensive, and remarkably effective. I publish them to benefit poor patients.

Minor Cold: If you are slightly infected with a cold, feel dizzy, tired, have a stuffy nose and runny nose, commonly known as a minor cold; you can cook a bowl of noodles, with two-thirds meat soup and one-third hot vinegar, add a lot of spicy chili ingredients, add a little green onion and ginger, and drink a cup of warm wine as a supplement, and you will sweat immediately and get better.

Prolonged Cough and Weakness Due to Cold: People with weak bodies and prolonged coughs are prone to catching a cold and coughing during major seasonal changes, such as the equinoxes and solstices. They often have a prolonged cough that does not heal. You should take three eggs, remove the yolks and keep the whites, put them in a bowl and mix them with sugar, then take a few slices of ginger and two qian of Jingjie and decoct them in boiling water. Then use this water to pour into the egg bowl, mix it, and take it. Take it once every morning and once before going to bed. It will be effective in one or two days.

Initial Dysentery: In the early stage of dysentery, cook one or two liang of wood ear, remove the water, put it in a bowl, mix it with fermented bean curd juice, add a little mountain pepper, and use it as a side dish. Eat it for several days in a row. Severe cases will be reduced, and mild cases will be cured immediately.

Prolonged Dysentery: For persistent dysentery, take pine resin and burn it, drip its oil onto the skin of a banana, add two pieces of fried scorched glutinous rice candy—that is, maltose—and decoct it and take it immediately. Also: five qian of Cao Guo peel, one liang of charcoal ginger, and five qian of fried scorched glutinous rice can also stop dysentery.

Abdominal Pain: If you have cold abdominal pain without chills or fever, take a dozen peppercorns, grind them into powder, and swallow them with hot soup.

Toothache: For those suffering from wind-heat toothache, grind calcined gypsum and white pepper into a fine powder; apply it to the teeth to relieve pain.

Yellow Water Scabies: Yellow water scabies is a terrible disease. You can boil mutton twice to promote suppuration and decay, and the scab will form in seven days.

Ear Sores: For children with sores in their ears, drip male chicken bile into the ears. After one or two days, the heat toxin will be completely removed, and the scab will form immediately; then moisturize it with vegetable oil.

Insomnia: Before going to bed, pour boiling water over ghee and add rock sugar; eating it is most effective for nourishing the heart and calming the nerves, and it is quite effective for treating insomnia.

Prevention: Prepare a bowl of clear vinegar, add salt, , garlic, and pepper, each in a small amount; take fresh and cut it into slices, immerse them in the bowl of vinegar; eat them from time to time, so you can rely on them to avoid the spread of the plague.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Essays

Killing Without a Blink

— Zhou Ge

In these times, what does killing a person or two matter? Under a single bomb, hundreds, even thousands die at once, and we regard it as if it were mere statistics, without being moved in the slightest. What is the reason for this? Clearly, war has made our hearts extremely cruel, hasn't it?

But are our hearts truly cruel? I think not! Perhaps when we see hundreds of thousands of deaths in the newspaper, the detailed, gruesome details are missing. If they were recorded, would we really cry out, "Ah! Ten thousand died!" in such a casual tone?

Erich Maria Remarque's "All Quiet on the Western Front," when brought to the silver screen, gave people a very deep impression of the cruelty of war. This is largely the reason why the warmongering Hitler wanted to ban it.

If we are indifferent to collective death (!), how much more so to individual death? We hear people say: so-and-so was shot to death in such-and-such a place, and we are not moved in the slightest. Yet, we often see in the newspaper that a robber, before being executed, is pale-faced, walks weakly, and is, of course, in a state of mental stupor. A priest is even praying for him, and this pitiful scene truly makes it hard to breathe when reading about it. Why do people have to kill people?

The so-called important criminal Hauptmann, of the Lindbergh kidnapping case, was killed by being electrocuted three times in the electric chair. Let us read the news report: "...The right leg of his pants was torn to facilitate the placement of the electrode. After Hauptmann was seated in the electric chair, the executioner Eieler and his assistant immediately wrapped the wet electrode around his body. Twelve witnesses and six journalists were in front of the electric chair, listening quietly to his last words... Then, he flipped the switch, and after a sound, Hauptmann's body curled forward..." Enough! "The wet electrode was wrapped around his body," "Hauptmann's body curled forward," and there were people listening quietly to his last words. What a great and solemn scene of watching death! I really can't bear to finish reading it.

Finally, I must state that I am not a humanitarian in the narrow sense. We know that these "people killing people" tragedies will not disappear until society is completely transformed. Let us strive to transform society to perfection!

Opium Den for Sale

— Ma

After navigating thirty li of waterway against the wind, the boat arrived at the tomb area, and the sun was already setting. If it were a smooth journey with the wind, it would have been time to turn back. My uncle was an old addict, and on the boat, he was already yawning incessantly. He hardly resembled someone who had travelled this waterway often, asking the boatmen whether they had passed the Ten Li Pavilion or the Wu Li Pond. It was as if the narrow cabin could not accommodate his slender body, and he kept shifting from the cabin to the front of the boat, and then to the bow. But at the bow, there was a strong wind, and the two boatmen were tightly gripping the oars and poles in the front and back, seemingly too busy to answer my uncle's questions. Despite their efforts, the boat seemed frozen in the middle of the river, not moving an inch. The banks were all fields, with nothing to see except for dilapidated thatched pavilions every five li, for the use of travelers to rest. Although I was also worried about when we would reach the tomb, as bandits often appeared on this waterway after dark, I did not have the courage to ask the boatmen, and what would be the use?

My uncle went from the cabin to the bow and back to the cabin a dozen times. He gradually became exhausted and lay down on the bunk, tapping his feet. He wanted me to search his briefcase to see if I could find something to satisfy his craving. He always carried this briefcase when he went out, and often hid a little bit of his private stash in the bottom or in the seams. But today, due to my grandmother's urging, he did not have time to prepare that most important nourishment. So he began to curse my grandmother. At that time, my uncle had completely lost his human rationality and was controlled by that poison.

When the boat arrived at the tomb area, he told me, "Ask the tomb keeper if you don't understand anything," and hurriedly went to the opium den for sale with a tenant farmer. After a full hour, the registration was complete, but my uncle still had not returned. The sky was gradually darkening. Since we could not sail at night, we naturally had to find a place to stay first. So I asked the tomb keeper to take me to the opium den for sale.

It was probably a cloth market. In a corner, there was a low-lying tiled house with an oil lamp at the door, with three red characters written on it: 售吸所 (Opium Den for Sale). It was said that it was open to the public. As I walked in, a thick smell of smoke assaulted my nose, almost causing me to gag. Walking into the inner room, it was completely filled with smoke. I only heard a hoarse voice calling out that the young nephew had arrived. At the same time, a hand pulled me over. When I bumped my buttocks against something hard, I realized that it was a wooden bed. My uncle was sleeping there with his eyes closed. My uncle was already fast asleep. The person who called me the young nephew called him awake. He immediately became energetic again. He asked me if the sacrifice was over and if the boatmen were ready to set sail.

I did not answer. The tomb keeper then said: "Second master, it's getting dark. Should we stay at the tomb house tonight or find an inn? I'll go back and prepare the bedding."

My uncle coughed, as if he didn't trust him, and said, "Is it already dark?" Then he nodded, "Prepare a bed for the young nephew."

Just as the tomb keeper walked out, two people staggered in, shouting at the door. The hoarse voice immediately greeted them with a smile, offering tea and cigarettes. The two people scanned the room and pointed at my uncle, asking him a question. He bowed and replied: "Don't you recognize him? This is the second gentleman. He has a license." My uncle also sat up from the bunk at that time. He then introduced the one in the lead: "This is Chief Zhu."

Chief Zhu and my uncle started talking and got along immediately. The two of them began to smoke at opposite ends of the bunk, as if they were old friends. The owner brought tea, handed over towels, and kept busy.

After eating dinner at the opium den for sale, my uncle said that he would stay there when the tomb keeper came to take me to sleep, and that he would call me when the boat was ready to sail tomorrow.

I did not sleep well that night. My nose felt blocked by something and was not very comfortable.

Disgusting Woman

— Yan

The spring breeze blew like a reptile, and Lilai, who had not slept all night, seemed to regain her spirits after getting into the car. She recalled what had happened last night, it seemed like a century ago, and she almost didn't believe that she would have fallen so low. She looked up at the sky, which was a azure blue. The sun was developing its heat, shining the world completely under its light, without baseness, without dirt. As Xinlai thought this, she felt as if she had been reborn. She opened her handbag, wanting to check her face in the small mirror, but when a roll of colorful banknotes reflected into her eyes, she sank into the carriage as if she had lost consciousness. "That disgusting woman!" It was as if countless venomous eyes were focused on her.

The car stopped in front of her house. She paid the fare and leaned against the door frame. She imagined her father's angry face and her mother's tearful sorrow. She wished that she could just die like this right now! So she closed her eyes, as if expecting the arrival of the god of death. But the door suddenly opened, and she fell into someone's arms; it was her mother.

Her mother had a sorrowful face, just as she had imagined. She had not raised a son, and she said that it was because she had committed sins in her previous life. But her husband did not think this way. He loved his daughter like a son. He sent his daughter to school. But in a war, he lost his job. Under the torment of difficult times, he was finally persuaded by a roommate to send his daughter to the dance hall. However, he told his daughter: This is a last resort. I don't want you to earn this kind of money to support me. As long as your father finds a job, you can still go to school. He patted his daughter's shoulder with shame. His daughter saw tears in her father's eyes for the first time.

So her daughter endured various insults and became a dancer. She turned from bright days to a dark hell. But she always remembered her father's words. She did not see herself as a dancer. She only went to earn every dance ticket in a legitimate way. She looked forward to the arrival of happiness, to being the daughter her father wanted her to be.

Now she cried in her mother's arms. She had disappointed her father too much, although it was not her own sin. In that dark hell, venomous beasts lurked everywhere. How could a girl resist the oppression of this harsh environment! She slowly followed her mother into the bedroom. Her father only looked at her whole body with fiery eyes, as if he wanted to see through the dirt on her body. Her mother held her daughter tightly and said gently: Ask her properly. You only have this one daughter!

"Hmph! I don't want her to see my face again. I don't have such a shameful daughter!" He searched in the drawer and took out a pair of scissors and threw them in front of his daughter: "Otherwise, just die for me!"

The daughter looked at her father's fiery eyes, and she couldn't help but cry again. How had her father taught her? She didn't want to explain to her father. She only hoped to die sooner. If her life didn't end, she would always be subjected to that kind of insult! She suddenly jumped out of her mother's arms, wanting to grab the scissors and commit suicide, so that she could keep a clean soul.

Her mother immediately stopped her daughter, stomping her feet and crying, "What sins did I commit in my previous life that even a daughter has to be forced to death!"

Thus, the father turned pale with anger, and pushed his daughter away frantically, almost like declaring war on an enemy. When the daughter fell to the corner, the banknotes in her handbag fell to the center of the room, the colorful banknotes like the faces of wild beasts.

The father's tears fell from his eyes again. He beat his head with his fists, like a madman, seeming to kick and trample on the scattered banknotes...

Nora (20)

— (Illustration by Wan Chao Chen) (Description by Xin Xin)

After Mrs. Lindon left, Helmer was being affectionate with Nora, when Dr. Rank came. Helmer: (muttering) Annoying, what's he doing here at this time? (aloud) Wait a moment! (opens the door) Come in, you're so good, never refusing to enter a house.

Dr. Rank happily enjoyed the evening. Before leaving, he asked for a cigar, which Nora lit for him. After saying "I hope you sleep well" to each other, he nodded and left.

Helmer went to open the mailbox. On the lock of the mailbox, he discovered Nora's hairpin.

After taking the letters back, they found Dr. Rank's calling card with a black cross drawn on it, a calling card foretelling his own death.

Although Nora had made up her mind to let Helmer see the letters, Helmer was very disappointed to receive the news of the death of his dying good friend, so he took the letters and went straight back to his room.

Cai Xiaofang's Mao Family Book

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening: "Night Rain on the Xiaoxiang"

Clouds swirl and envelop the curtained chamber. The moonlight is dim and hazy.

Page 19

Page 20

Page 21

A thick haze surrounds the Xiaoxiang Pavilion. A few cold and desolate green gauze windows. The whistling sound of a thousand tall bamboo stalks. Several branches of thin crabapple trees with green grass. A listless and melancholic young woman. Two small, lonely maids. All one sees is, a thin, sheer silk dress. A sallow, thin, and wan face. Eyes gazing, eyes filled with sorrow. Brows furrowed, brows filled with resentment. Quietly sitting on a Xiangfei couch. Softly leaning against an ivory bed. A dimly lit, half-burnt candle tear. A cold, icy, half cup of medicine. Pitifully, she gasps for breath. Her heart is restless. She coughs repeatedly. Tears stream down her face. Bloodstains soak through her thin silk dress. Her feelings are intense and apprehensive, sighing again and again, lamenting her desolate situation. Pitiful me, separated from my homeland. Lonely and isolated in a foreign land. The road is long, thousands of miles away. The white expanse makes it impossible to see my old home. A vague feeling that the Yellow Springs are near. It would be better to seek an early demise. Look at her, spirit dazed, all thoughts empty. Lonely shadow, all things are vicissitudes of life. All one sees, the night is deep, the night color is miserable. The sound is quiet, the sound of sorrow is long. All one hears is, the wind rustling, the wind cold. The rain is drizzling, the rain is heavy. Dripping sound of the copper pot that never stops. The clanging sound of the iron horse. The gentle thud of the wind moving the curtain hooks. The pattering of raindrops hitting the cold windows. Ding-dong, the bell rings three times. Dong-dong, the signal tower strikes the fifth watch. That concubine is, unable to withstand the cold wind. The long night, the night rain breaks her heart. From now on, the sickness will enter her very bones.

Xu Wenbi's Opening

Hangye (1180) 11:15 AM to 12:00 PM

Opening: Romance of the Western Chamber "The Long Pavilion"

Parting and reunion, joy and sorrow, with a cup of wine. A banquet is set up at the long pavilion to bid farewell to the autumn scholar. Only because the Madam forced him to take the test. He had to go to the capital for a trip. Only seen outside the sky the green clouds with hating shadow. Yellow flowers filled the ground with sad thoughts. I thought Liang Hao ascended to heaven at an old age. Sooner or later, it is difficult to defy the mandate of heaven. I steadily climb the osmanthus tree in the moon palace. I vow not to return without a name on the golden list. Brother ah. Take care of yourself in the windy and snowy inns. Do not rush your horse on the long journey. The horse walks slowly. The carriage closely follows. The setting sun urges with a whip. Do not think of the beautiful spring scenery of the capital. Return to your hometown with honor and glory. Good things are often difficult, as the saying goes. Do not hang misfortune on your chest. You should entrust your message to the fish in the river and the geese in the sky. I eagerly await the good news of the gilded announcement. Inexhaustible. Thousands of words of concern. That forbidden. Disturbed dust blown to face. The most painful thing in life is separation. I will send you a thousand miles and we must separate. Two hearts will follow each other in dreams tonight.

Aftersound

The Hanba Society has been broadcasting the four-act tragedy "Thunderstorm" on the Mainland Radio Station for days.

The two stage songs distributed by the Chongsheng Society in the first batch were sold out, and the second batch is being reprinted. Those who wrote letters to request the songs will receive them in the coming days. The new address of the society is 314 Qipu Road.

Movie News

Star Miscellany

Hu Die's health has gradually recovered after undergoing a tonsillectomy, and she will soon be able to return to work on the film set.

Gu Meijun and Zhu Qiuhong play a pair of dancers in "New and Old Shanghai."

"Peaches and Plums Compete for Beauty" has three moving songs: "Shattered Jade Balustrade," "Youth Misspent," and "Peaches and Plums Compete for Beauty." The first song is sung by Ye Qiuxin, and the latter two are sung by Gu Lanjun.

"The Fugitive of Love" has been decided to be renamed "Women's Rights."

The special oversized issue of Star Bi-Monthly is making every effort to solicit contributions from all sides.

"New Book Shanghai" received the Film Script Review Committee: "... The play depicts the suffering of the city people's lives in the social depression. The plot and meaning are very profound ... It is hoped that it will be properly filmed to achieve perfection."

Wu Cun's "Eternal Smile" is being prepared for filming.

Lianhua Side Stories

"Waves Washing Sand" has two major contributions to the technique of national film production: one is artificial fog and the other is underwater photography.

It often snows in June on the film set, but now it is not summer, and lotuses are in full bloom in the general's mansion in "Back to Nature."

Fei Mu's new work can be divided into acts, and the filming date should not be far away.

In the filming of the village scene in "The Lost Lamb," a large amount of explosives was used to bomb the entire village. Zheng Junli and five extras playing peasants were slightly injured.

It is said that Cai Chusheng's work after "The Lost Lamb" is titled "Wang Laowu."

Three modern men, Han Langan, Liu Jijun, and Yin Xiucen, watched Chaplin's "Modern Times" together one evening, but had no comments after watching it.

Zhang Yi, Shang Guanwu, and Zhang Zhizhi are the three soldiers in Yang Xiaozhong's new work "Three Battles Seven."

The scene in "The Lost Lamb" where children play shadow puppets is extremely ingenious in its filming technique, which is still new in domestic films, and is a creation of director Cai Chusheng's painstaking effort.

The large feather fan used by Li Lili in "Back to Nature" is extremely beautiful and was purchased from a large company for 115 gold yuan. It is said that this fan comes from Paris, and Shanghai has only this one.

Cai Chusheng attaches great importance to the dubbing of "The Lost Lamb," and has been discussing it with Ren Guang and An E in recent days. The dubbing can begin in the next few days.

Sun Yu's works have a large youth audience. "Back to Nature" is an even more meaningful and interesting work after "The Highway." It can be predicted that this film will be a sensation.

Zhang Zhizhi, who plays a general of the army in the warlord era in "Back to Nature," borrowed the medals he wore during filming from a certain important person out of office. Not forged.

Yisheng Youth Issue Published

The Youth Issue of Yisheng, Volume 2, Number 2, edited by Chen Jiazhen, was published a few days ago. Due to the special increase in materials, it was delayed for two days. The compilation is full of poetic meaning. Whether it is text, photographs, or comics, they are all very interesting and full of life. The main items include Everyone's Love, Li Lili's 24-Hour Special, Wang Renmei's Sheffler Sketch, Hu Ping's Nickname, The Arrangement of Female Stars' Rooms, and Chen Jiazhen's Creative Joy Troupe, etc. The price is only two cents per copy.
